Wang Chonghui Discusses Suiyuan and Foreign Affairs, Considers Whether to Suspend Diplomatic Negotiations, and Whether the Suiyuan Incident Can Be Appealed to the League of Nations According to the Covenant

Dr. Wang Chonghui, former judge of the International Court of Justice, returned north to Shanghai earlier this month after representing the central government at the state funeral of the late President Huk of Mecca in Guangdong. He is still staying in Shanghai. Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, visited him the day before yesterday to exchange views on national affairs. Yesterday morning, Wang met with reporters from the 新声社 (New Voice Society) at his residence and made the following remarks on national affairs:

Not an Inch of Territory Can Be Ceded Again

In answering questions from reporters, Wang first mentioned the invasion of Suiyuan by the bandits and puppet troops, saying that the lost territory has not yet been recovered, and now there is another invasion by the bandits and puppets. Where is the background? The world knows. At this moment, we must not retreat again, and not an inch of territory can be lost. Reports say that troops from a certain country are moving from Rehe towards Chahar and Suiyuan. Although the Japanese authorities still repeatedly deny participating in the Suiyuan incident, it must be known that participation is one thing, and the Japanese side will never publicly admit it. Otherwise, it would be tantamount to declaring war.

Stop Negotiations Immediately

Continuing, he talked about the Sino-Japanese diplomatic negotiations. Now that the Suiyuan incident has occurred, should we formally announce the suspension of negotiations immediately? This depends on how far Foreign Minister Zhang and the Japanese Ambassador have negotiated in the past. Because I do not know the content, I am not in a position to arbitrarily advocate for it. When President Sun came to visit yesterday, he also mentioned it, but he did not know the details because he had been away from the capital for a long time. Our views on the Suiyuan incident and foreign affairs cannot be recommended to the government until after a thorough study.

Can Appeal to the League of Nations

Then the reporter asked whether, since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, the Suiyuan incident can still be appealed to the League of Nations. Wang replied that according to Article 17 of the League of Nations Covenant, it is still possible to submit it to the League of Nations. However, since the League of Nations failed to handle the September 18th Incident, and recently failed to handle the Italy-Abyssinia dispute effectively, the League of Nations itself has lost its prestige and has no power at all. Therefore, whether there will be any results if the Suiyuan incident is submitted is still a question. But the League of Nations is now engaged in amending the Covenant, trying to extricate itself, and hoping to restore its former prestige.

Observe the German-Japanese Alliance

The reporter further asked about his observations on the German-Japanese alliance. According to him, both Germany and Japan are still denying this matter, and it is not yet known what the content is. According to my observation, if there is such a thing, its content must be complicated and not just an alliance. Japan is simply trying to use the situation in Europe to contain the Far East. Wang said at the end that he would go to the capital when necessary, but he has no such preparation at the moment. His nasal disease has improved significantly and he is temporarily stopping treatment for two weeks before taking another X-ray to see if it is completely cured.

Labor Unrest in Japanese Cotton Mills, Party and Government Agencies Mediate All Night, As a Result, the Kiwa Three Factories and One or Two Places in the Toyoda Factory Are Scheduled to Resume Work One After Another Today and Tomorrow, Both Internal and External Factories Petition the Social Affairs Bureau, Labor Unrest Occurred Again Yesterday in the Nichihua Third and Fourth Factories

According to the 大公社 (Da Gong News Agency), after the Party and government agencies mediated the labor unrest in the Kiwa Three Factories in West Shanghai, eight settlement conditions were signed. All workers are scheduled to resume work this morning, and the Toyoda Factory is scheduled to start work tomorrow morning. The labor side issued a resumption of work declaration. Representatives from various internal and external cotton factories petitioned the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. A strike occurred again yesterday afternoon at the Nichihua Cotton Mill. The Japanese spinning industry sent personnel to Shanghai to investigate the truth of the labor unrest. The report is as follows:

幕和 (Kiwa) Cotton Mill

All the workers of the Japanese-owned Kiwa First, Second, and Third Factories on Route Robert sought to increase wages and proposed seven conditions to improve their treatment. The factory refused to accept, leading to a strike. They also fired six people, including the meal contractor Wang Han. Yesterday morning, the workers supported their representatives and petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting that the factory be notified to settle their wages and leave the factory to return to their hometowns, unwilling to work in the factory again. Therefore, the labor unrest intensified. In order to resolve the dispute as soon as possible, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent Wang Xianqing, director of the mediation section of the Third Department, together with Wu Wenbang, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, and Tan Baoshou, director of the Caojiadu Branch of the Public Security Bureau, to the factory to negotiate. After Director Wang earnestly persuaded both labor and management from the government's standpoint, eight settlement conditions were finally signed at 7:30 PM, declaring a resolution.

Signed Conditions

(1) All workers will receive a 5% wage increase starting from the first half of November. (2) Day and night shift workers will each have 30 minutes of rest during meal times. (3) Night workers on Saturdays must not have their work extended. For extended working hours, wages will be increased according to factory regulations. (4) When hiring workers, workers recruited in the workshop should be given priority. If there are no suitable people in the workshop, the factory may recruit others. (5) The labor side requests that compensation and allowances be paid monthly. Both sides will follow the method decided by the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China to ensure uniformity. (6) The six cooks, including Chen Guoyu, Wang Han, Li Baoquan, Sun Dequan, Zhou Daosheng, and Yu Shoufan, will still be allowed to reside in the workshop. (7) The factory must not dismiss workers or expel cooks from the workshop without reason. (8) The labor side will resume work uniformly at 6:00 AM on the 24th of this month (today). Capital representatives were 梠久治 (Taro Kuju), labor representatives were He Hanru, Zhou Daosheng, and nine others, Social Affairs Bureau representative was Wang Xianqing, Municipal Party Department representative was Wu Wenbang, and Public Security Bureau Caojiadu Branch Director was 译葆 (Bao Yi).

Internal and External Cotton Mills

After the labor unrest occurred in the Japanese-owned Internal and External Cotton Mills No. 1, 2, 5, 6, 7, 8, and 9, the workers put forward seven conditions (the contents of the conditions are the same as those of other factories) and demanded that the factory accept them, but they were rejected and the issue remained unresolved. Yesterday morning at 9:15, more than ten workers from the factory went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to petition. Wang Xianqing, director of the mediation section of the Third Department, met with them and, after inquiring about the situation, promised to negotiate with the factory. A second batch of more than 20 worker representatives then petitioned the Social Affairs Bureau at 10:30, and Wang Xianqing again met with them and promised to contact the factory about the workers' demands. They dispersed at around 11:00 AM.

Situation of Various Factories

The Internal and External Cotton Mills No. 1 and No. 2 on Robert Road have a total of more than 1,400 workers. More than 100 day shift workers entered the factory to work yesterday morning, and 550 night shift workers entered the factory to work. Mills No. 5, 6, 7, and 3 on West Suzhou Road have a total of more than 3,600 workers. About 300 day shift workers entered the factory to work yesterday morning, and 600 night shift workers entered the factory to work. Mill No. 8 on Gordon Road has a total of more than 1,600 workers. More than 210 day shift workers entered the factory to work yesterday morning, and 400 night shift workers entered the factory to work. Mill No. 9 on Mackinnon Road has a total of more than 1,200 workers. About 150 day shift workers entered the factory to work yesterday morning, and 320 night shift workers entered the factory to work.

Nichihua Factories

The Nichihua Third and Fourth Cotton Mills at No. 500 Robert Road in West Shanghai employ a total of 2,051 male and female workers. Fortunately, the factory was not involved in the strike that occurred in various Japanese cotton mills in West Shanghai this time. However, at 3:15 PM yesterday, when 1,050 day shift workers were working, two female workers in the winding room were repairing their machines, which were damaged. A Japanese supervisor saw this and suspected that the two female workers were closing the machines to instigate a strike. He immediately telephoned the Xiaoshadu Road police station, which immediately sent four Western detectives and 50 Chinese and Western detectives to rush to the factory and drive all the workers out of the factory, thus causing a labor unrest. The night shift workers also expressed dissatisfaction because of the arbitrary oppression by the factory and did not enter the factory to work.

Toyoda Cotton Mill

After more than 4,500 male and female workers in the Toyoda First and Second Factories at Zhongshan Road Bridge went on a joint strike on the 17th of this month, the unrest was extremely serious. Du Yuesheng, President of the Local Association of this city, concerned that the dispute was persistent and that both labor and management suffered losses, and also affected social security, specially accompanied Qian Xinzhi, a leader in the banking industry, to mediate. After repeatedly visiting Tatsichiro Funatsu, President of the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China, and the heads of the factories to discuss the matter, six conditions were decided. At the same time, they also advised the worker representatives and finally reached a resolution. All workers are scheduled to enter the factory on Wednesday (tomorrow) to resume work. At the same time, the factory will also reorganize the internal machinery of the factory and decide to start work as scheduled.

Resolved Conditions

(1) Release the arrested workers. (2) Increase wages by 9% (those with too low wages in normal times will be increased appropriately according to the above example). (3) Monthly party wages will be changed to a monthly incentive system. (4) For working 12 hours on Sundays, if the workload is busy and exceeds 12 hours, the wages will be increased according to the earned wages, and a night porridge will be provided. Those who do not work will be allowed to rest. (5) Workers must not be dismissed without cause. (6) All striking workers will resume work.

General News

After the labor unrest occurred successively in the Japanese-owned cotton mills in Shanghai, the Japanese government and public opinion paid close attention. Now Toyoda Risaburo, President of Toyoda, and Shigeru Oshima and other senior members of the Japanese spinning industry have arrived in Shanghai on the Shanghai No. 9 to investigate the truth of the strikes in various factories and to inspect the damage to the Toyoda Second Factory. They also attended the meeting of the Japanese Spinning Industry Association in China held yesterday afternoon to discuss solutions, and expressed their gratitude to Du for his mediation.

The Sino-French Friendship Association Welcomed the French Ambassador Yesterday, Wang Chonghui, Li Shizeng, and Others Participated, The Ambassador Hosted a Banquet for His Country's Nationals Yesterday

The Sino-French Friendship Association held a grand tea party at the association's clubhouse at No. 577 Route Lafayette at 5:30 PM yesterday to welcome the French Ambassador to China, Mr. Naciagy. Chinese attendees included Chairman Zhao Zhiyou, Wang Chonghui, Li Shizeng, Wei Daoming, Zheng Yuxiu, Zhang Yichu, Zhuang Zhihuan Qi Zhi, Wu Kai, Hu Wenyao, Wang Rongqing, Liu Dao, Xiao Jinfang, Feng Zhizhong, Lu Shidao, Nong Ruhui, and Shen Zhongjun, among others. French attendees included the Vice-President of the Association, Xue Fan, the Consul General in Shanghai, Badas, Consul Bujinhua, the Director-General of the French Concession, Fan Erdi, the Commissioner of Police, Faber, Deputy Commissioner Gaibier, Political Director Sally, Finance Director Dai Qierdi, Education Director Gao Boai, and President Cai Ermeng of the Aurora University Law School, among other male and female members and guests, totaling more than 100 people. Zhao Zhiyou delivered a welcome speech on behalf of the association, first describing the work of the association since its establishment, and discussing the relationship between Sino-French friendship, etc. The Ambassador then replied with a speech of thanks, saying that France and its people like to associate with friendly countries and peoples, and the establishment of the association is enough to help achieve this desire. He will do his best to promote the best cooperation between the two countries and their peoples, etc. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM. Afterwards, Ambassador Naciagy himself hosted a banquet at the 公馆马路外滩 (Bund) at 8:30 PM to entertain the scholars and merchants of his country in Shanghai (previously mistakenly reported as a banquet for Chinese and foreign officials), inquiring about the situation of the scholars and merchants. He is scheduled to go to the capital next week and will return to Shanghai again.

Next Year's British Coronation: British Community in Shanghai Prepares Celebrations

Next May marks the start of the coronation ceremonies for the new British Emperor. In the United Kingdom, preparations are already underway in full swing. The British community in Shanghai has recently begun planning various celebratory activities. It is said that the Shanghai Municipal Council has agreed to lend the Jiaozhou Road Park in West Shanghai for the British community children to hold a garden party during the British Emperor's coronation period next year.

New and Old Commanders of the Japanese Marines in Shanghai Replaced Yesterday; Kondo Sadakane to Return Home on the 27th to Assume Command of the Yokosuka Naval Garrison

The new commander of the Japanese Marines in Shanghai, Okawauchi Denzichi, arrived in Shanghai on the 22nd from Japan and stayed at the Hoyo-kan Hotel on Peng Road. According to the Japanese Embassy Office, Okawauchi went to the Marines Headquarters on Jiangwan Road yesterday morning around 9 o'clock to complete the handover procedures with the outgoing commander, Kondo Hideketsu, officially announcing his assumption of office. He is scheduled to inspect all Marines stationed in Shanghai on the 25th. As for the outgoing commander Kondo, he is scheduled to return to Japan on the 27th aboard the Shanghai Maru to assume his new position as commander of the Yokosuka Naval Garrison in Japan.

Li Gongpu and Six Others Arrested Yesterday; Court Hearing Held Yesterday, Temporarily Granted Bail, Continued Hearing Postponed

According to the Central News Agency, sources revealed that Li Gongpu, Wang Zaoshi, Sha Qianli, and six others organized illegal groups, colluded with communists, incited strikes, class boycotts, and market shutdowns, conspired to disrupt public order, and attempted to overthrow the government. The government authorities, based on the Emergency Law for Punishing Offenses Against the Republic of China, cooperated with the concession police to arrest them and separately sent them to the Special District Court. A court hearing was held yesterday morning. Due to the seriousness of the case, a thorough investigation is pending, and the continued hearing has been postponed. They were temporarily granted bail pending further inquiry.

Huang Fu's Condition Worsens; Urinary Retention, Abdominal Distension, and Sharp Decline in Appetite; Doctors Currently Performing Bowel Movement and Other Procedures

State Councilor Huang Fu has been receiving treatment for stomach problems at the Hong En Hospital. After undergoing surgery by Western doctors and treatment by Fan Shisheng, he switched to traditional Chinese medicine. His condition had gradually improved, and dangerous signs had decreased. However, due to his advanced age and weakened blood, he required a long period of recuperation. According to a Xinxin News Agency reporter, in addition to continuing treatment by Fan Shisheng, Western doctors were also examining Huang's condition from time to time, hoping to combine Western and traditional Chinese medicine for a speedy recovery. Unexpectedly, in recent days, he suddenly suffered from urinary retention. Despite several attempts to induce bowel movements, no results were seen, leading to abdominal distension and a sharp decline in appetite. The surgically opened abdomen showed cracks due to the distension. Therefore, doctors are currently performing corrective surgery and researching methods to induce bowel movements, hoping that his improving condition will not take another turn for the worse.

Income Tax Rate: Promulgated Based on Economic Conditions. The "Da Mei Wan Bao" Commentary Contains Much Misunderstanding. The "Continental Daily News" Has Already Published Articles Refuting It. The Income Tax Affairs Office Does Not Attach Importance to It.

Central News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance is levying income tax. Because it is a new undertaking, it is being implemented gradually. The regulations are being formulated in detail, and opinions are being collected from all parties. Recently, the "Da Mei Wan Bao" published an editorial criticizing the tax regulations promulgated by the Ministry and comparing them with the situation in the United States. There are many discrepancies with the actual situation. The English-language "Continental Daily News" then wrote an article to refute it. A reporter yesterday specifically inquired with the Income Tax Affairs Office and received a detailed explanation. The key points of the two newspapers and their discussions are recorded below.

English "Da Mei Evening News" Editorial

On the 11th of this month, the English "Da Mei Wan Bao" published an editorial criticizing the newly implemented Chinese income tax system. It also used charts to compare the tax systems of the United States and the Philippines in detail. Summarizing the details, there are approximately five points: 1. Under the Chinese income tax system, interest income, regardless of size, is taxed at a rate of 5%. However, the tax rate on salary income is higher than that on interest income (for example, salary income above 700 is taxed at a rate exceeding 5%). 2. The tax rate on middle and lower salary income increases too quickly, while higher salary income is treated preferentially. 3. Regardless of the taxpayer's family burden, the tax-free amount is uniformly set at 30 yuan. 4. Lower-level workers with a monthly salary of more than 30 yuan, such as servants, mechanics, chauffeurs, clerks, shop assistants, etc., are not exempt from tax. 5. The monthly micro-collection costs of Chinese income tax are enormous, and it is feared that income will not cover expenses.

Refutation by the English-language "Continental Daily News"

Recently, the English-language "Continental Daily News" published an article by Li Wu, severely refuting the points raised by the "Da Mei Wan Bao." The key points are as follows: 1. The economic situations of China and the United States are very different, and the living standards of the two countries are also different. Very few individuals in China have a monthly salary income exceeding 1,500 yuan. The "Da Mei Wan Bao"'s so-called middle and lower salary income almost includes all levels of salary income in the country. The increase rate with the rise of income is slightly the same, so the statement that the highest salary income is treated preferentially is completely unfounded. 2. The lowest individual monthly salary income in China is far less than that in the United States. The starting point for salary income tax in the United States is 1,000 yuan in Chinese currency per month. Individuals in China with a monthly salary income below 1,000 yuan account for more than 95%. If the standard for salary income must be the same as in the United States, then it will be impossible to implement salary income tax in China. 3. Lower-level workers in China, such as servants and mechanics, rarely have a monthly salary income exceeding the tax-free amount (30 yuan). Therefore, in reality, these people are all exempt from tax. 4. China adopts a withholding system. Although it is collected monthly, all expenses are extremely limited. 5. Very few individuals in China have a monthly salary income exceeding 700 yuan, and it can be said that there are extremely few exceeding 1,500 yuan. Therefore, the actual highest tax rate on salary income is no more than 5%. The "Da Mei Wan Bao"'s assertion that China's income tax treats interest income and salary income unequally is not a problem.

Opinions of the Income Tax Affairs Office

The reporter believes that both sides of the debate are related to academics, so he visited someone from the Income Tax Affairs Office about this matter. According to him, the reports from both newspapers have been given deep attention. From his personal opinion, the economic level of China is very different from that of the United States and the Philippines. The "Da Mei Wan Bao" did not investigate this point in detail, which is due to a lack of understanding of the Chinese situation. China's family system and property system are different from those in the West. It is impossible to use the situation in Shanghai or other cities as an example for the whole country. For example, children having no private property is an old Chinese etiquette. Even today, large families and those who live together in clans still adhere to this virtue. Therefore, able-bodied men in the eyes of Europeans and Americans are independent, and their elderly parents are dependent, but in the eyes of old Chinese etiquette, these able-bodied men are dependent, and their economic independence is still in the hands of their parents. This is all clear evidence. As for labor income, the rate should be lower than capital income, although this is an indisputable theory. However, China has concessions and foreign banks, and whether the interest income of foreign banks can be taxed uniformly has not been resolved. If China legislates to adopt a progressive system for interest income, it would be tantamount to encouraging Chinese capital to flee, and foreign banks would take advantage of this opportunity to absorb capital. (For example, the ordinary interest rate for deposits in Chinese banks is 4%, while the ordinary interest rate for deposits in foreign banks is 3%. If the Chinese interest income tax exceeds 1%, Chinese capital will inevitably be at risk of fleeing.) China currently only extracts three types of income from various incomes to levy income tax. Since the taxable object is not all of the income, the deduction of personal living expenses and the tax exemption for those who depend on others cannot completely follow the example of Europe and the United States. In short, income tax is an extremely complex and scientific tax rule. In terms of the progress of income tax history in various countries, it has not been achieved overnight. The current Chinese tax system is similar to the British classified income tax system and will need to be gradually improved in the future. Although the arguments of foreign scholars are worthy of reference, they are ultimately not worth emphasizing.

Major Fire in Pudong Yesterday Morning: Five Houses Destroyed, Telephone Lines Cut Off, Girl Lin Bao Tragically Burned to Death, Corpse Like Charred Coal.

At 1:55 AM yesterday morning, a sudden fire broke out between Zhang Yongxing's cake shop, numbered 200 on Dongchang Road, Dongchang Lane, Pudong, and the adjacent 202, Wu Longtai. At that time, there were few pedestrians on the road. By the time it was discovered, it had become a prairie fire. After the flames burst out of the storefront, they became even more rampant. The telephone pole opposite was also scorched and caught fire, instantly cutting off the main line connecting Pudong and Puxi, resulting in a temporary situation.

Quite Critical

The Pudong District Fire Brigade nearby immediately drove to the scene to rescue. However, there was no water source there, so they connected 30 five-zhang-long hoses to the Huangpu River, which took a lot of trouble to draw water for firefighting. At that time, the north wind was urgent, and the fire was fueled by the wind, and its momentum became even greater. The raging flames soared into the sky, causing nearby residents to be panic-stricken. For a time, moving furniture and objects filled the road, causing the order.

Quite Chaotic

The police and corps organs dispatched troops to the scene to suppress the situation, persuading onlookers to retreat to a corner so that firefighters could calmly carry out rescue operations. After an hour of burning, all five of the buildings in that block of city buildings were completely destroyed and spread to the houses in the first lane of Houshu Lane. Firefighters urgently changed their plan and requested that the water patrol team of the dragon head be sent to the police station, circling to the lane, and the houses in the second lane were.

Desperately Saved

After another hour, five houses in the first lane were also burned down one after another, and the fire gradually weakened. At that time, the fire brigade inspector Wang Zhenya was carrying the dragon head hose and was about to go to the depths of the fire in the lane to water. When he walked to the door of the destroyed No. 9, the wall suddenly collapsed, and Wang was unable to avoid it, and his body was crushed by the wall bricks.

Injured

Fortunately, all the firefighters immediately tried to rescue him, and his left hand had been seriously injured and it was difficult to bend it. He was urgently sent to Dr. Wang Xiongfei for treatment. Because the injury was not serious, he could still walk after bandaging. The fire lasted for about two hours, and a total of ten buildings were destroyed, including Wu Longtai's clothing store at No. 202, Zhang Yongxing's cake shop at No. 200, Shi Deji's buying and selling shop at No. 198, No. 196.

Jiang Jingshan and others' five buildings, and Gao Yuqing at No. 5, Lin Genda at No. 6, Tang Duanfang at No. 7, Li Ronghua at No. 8, and Shengneng Art Institute at No. 9 in Dongchang Lane, a total of ten buildings. The victims included more than 20 households, including two landlords and three tenants. The loss of houses and property was about 30,000 yuan. Also, Zhang Xichun, the owner of Zhang Yongxing's cake shop.

His adopted daughter, Lin Bao, was only twelve years old. When the fire broke out, she was sound asleep and could not escape, and was tragically burned to death. Until 2 PM yesterday afternoon, after the embers of the fire were completely extinguished, the girl's body was found after opening the rubble. It was charred like charcoal and unbearable to look at. The Pudong Branch then summoned Lu Shunlong, the map reporter of the area, to report to the court for inspection this morning. As for the Pudong Telephone Bureau, it also repaired the Pudong West.

The main line of communication was restored at noon yesterday. There are various rumors about the cause of the fire. Afterwards, according to Wu Liansheng, the local owner of the clothing store, who surrendered to the Pudong Branch, he claimed that the cake shop next door would start a fire to steam cakes at about 1 AM every day. The stove was close to the wall, and there was a lot of rice straw piled up on the mezzanine floor of his shop, so it was suspected that the fire was caused by the heat. The director considered it necessary to investigate and ordered it to be sent to the main bureau for disposition. It is heard that all the victims, except for the residents in the lane, have fire insurance.

Dadong Pharmacy Forgery of Medicines: Huang Futang Sentenced to One Year and Six Months

Dadong Pharmacy on Guangdong Road, because it specializes in forging the products of various pharmacies and counterfeiting trademarks, was recently discovered by Huaan Pharmacy on Hubei Road that Dadong Pharmacy has forged Huaan's quit smoking medicine, Black Sea Star, for mixed sale, damaging the business, etc. The case was reported to the General Patrol Room, which sent Detective Feng Zhiming to Dadong Pharmacy to copy more than ten boxes of various forged medicines, and arrested Manager Huang Futang, Accountant Jing Gengxing, and Shop Assistant Chen Xingguan. The three were escorted to the First Special Court. After several trials, the case has been concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Pan Zhenyang went to the Second Criminal Court to announce the judgment. The main text of the judgment reads: Huang Futang is sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment and fined 2,000 yuan for continuously forging registered trademarks with the intention of deceiving others. If the fine is converted into labor service, the amount for one day is determined by the ratio of 2,000 yuan to the number of days in six months. Jing Gengxing is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for helping to forge registered trademarks. Chen Xingguan is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for continuously helping to forge registered trademarks. The forged trademark medicines, such as Black Sea Star, are confiscated according to the list. The incidental civil lawsuit in this case is transferred to the Civil Court of this court.

Enmity Due to Gambling: Hua Shihao is Chopped to Death. The Murderer, Yang Hanzhang, Admits Without Hesitation. The Corpse of Hua was Inspected by the Court Yesterday.

Hua Shihao, courtesy name Zhao Kun, a Hubei native who was a teacher at the Jiujiang County Martial Arts Hall and a martial arts instructor at the Independent First Brigade Headquarters of the Marine Corps, lived at No. 51, Jiahe Lane, 81 Hedder Road. However, No. 46 of the lane was the clubhouse of the Hubei Fellow Association, so Hua often went there to play. On the 14th of this month, Hua Shihao had a conflict with Yang Hanzhang, a Hubei native living in the association, due to gambling in the fellow association. The two parties broke up unhappily, accumulating deep hatred. Yang Hanzhang bought two sharp axes on Minguo Road the day before and hid them on his body. At 10:10 PM, he ambushed at the entrance of Jiahe Lane. When he saw Hua Shihao arriving, he suddenly stepped forward, drew out the axe, and chopped down several times on the head, causing Hua to fall to the ground with injuries, and blood gushing like a spring. Yang then abandoned one axe, carried one axe and fled. At the intersection of Gu Xu Road and Haig Road, he was discovered by Indian Constable No. 311, who chased and captured Yang and brought him, along with the axe, to the Jing'an Temple Police Station. Detective Zhang Liang was dispatched to send the injured man to Renji Hospital. Due to the severity of the injuries and excessive blood loss, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at about 3 AM the day before. The body was sent to the coroner's office for examination. Yesterday morning, Yang Hanzhang was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Attorney Wang Yaotang filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 271 of the Criminal Law for murder and presented the case, requesting a postponement. When questioning Yang Hanzhang, he confessed without hesitation. Judge Huang ordered Yang to be detained for seven days for further interrogation. Meanwhile, Prosecutor Zhang went to the coroner's office to examine the body and determined that Hua Shihao had been chopped to death before death by an axe. The body was handed over to his wife, Hua Wang, who signed a bond to claim the body for burial.

Tiecheng, with his humble ability, believes that secular celebrations are not enough to promote the virtues of the worthy and show longevity. Therefore, he suggests fundraising to decorate the Longhua Scenic Area in this city (see the following items for details), hoping to use local scenic spots to wish Mr. Wang endless life, which is based on Mr. Wang's usual belief in the piety of self-cultivation and expanded into the merit of offering and construction. It is also what Mr. Wang would be happy to hear and silently approve of, isn't it? (1) Repair the Longhua Temple Pagoda for visitors from China and abroad to admire. (2) Build three rooms near the temple, named Wang Jushi Hall, with stone carvings of Mr. Wang's paintings displayed in it, or build a pavilion named Jushi Pavilion, or even call it Yiting. (3) Plant 10,000 peach trees in the Longhua area to embellish the scenery. (4) If there is surplus money, it should be stored as a foundation for repairing houses and planting trees.

Ye Qinghua Accused of Marriage and Rape Fraud, Continued Hearing. Mutual Accusations Make the Case Exceptionally Complex. Court Orders Further Summons of Witnesses for Questioning.

abandoned her,

Police officers took the three women, Wu, Yang, and Chen, to the police station for questioning, and then ordered Yang and Chen

to be fined and reprimanded.

Later, Wu, due to her injuries, sought medical treatment at the Jiangwan Women and Children's Education and Rehabilitation Center. She also filed another complaint with the Second Special District Court, accusing Yang Zhuxia, also known as Lanxiang, and Chen Rong of assault, requesting investigation. On the 15th of last month, Presiding Judge Zhang Chaozuo summoned the defendant. The plaintiff did not appear due to her injuries, only the defendant Ye Qinghua appeared in court. After questioning, the court announced a postponement for further hearing. The circumstances of Yang Zhuxia and Chen Rong also filing a complaint with the Second Special District Criminal Court, accusing Wu Yu of assault, having been summoned several times, but Wu Yu

not appearing due to her injuries, and the postponement of various matters, have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday, Presiding Judge Sun Pengxian resumed the hearing at the Second Criminal Court. Wu Yu's complaint against Ye Qinghua, Yang Zhuxia, and Chen Rong for offenses against public morals and assault were consolidated for trial. The plaintiffs Ye Qinghua and Yang Zhuxia, along with their lawyer, appeared in court. Chen Rong did not appear. The court announced a new trial. According to Wu Yu's statement, she accused the defendant of marriage fraud, rape, and abandonment, and presented letters previously given to her by Ye as evidence. She also claimed that Ye had previously promised to marry her and that they already had three children, the oldest being five years old, who had been

taken by Ye to a friend.

She was also tricked into deceiving his brother, and asked her to sign a separation agreement. At the time, he said he had no wife. Ye testified that his relationship with Wu was a cohabitation and that they had already separated. He had a wife, Yang Lanxiang, whom he married in Xiamen in the 8th year of the Republic of China. He had a relationship with the plaintiff in the 20th year of the Republic of China. She knew he had a wife and was very close to his wife, and they had exchanged letters. Yang Zhuxia testified that Ye Qinghua was her husband and that she married Ye when she was 19 years old. Ye Qinghua also testified that on the 13th of last month, he was in Nanjing and returned to Shanghai by night train. He learned of the summons and went to the court to retrieve it the next day. He denied

colluding with his wife to beat Wu. Wu Yu claimed that Ye Xiping and the tea boy from Number 18 saw Ye outside the Dacheng Apartment. The court showed the separation agreement to Wu to see if it was indeed the agreement. After Wu read it, she said, "It is my signature, but there is no stamp, and there are two clauses added: 'Before I have a fixed occupation, Ye will give me 50 yuan per month for living expenses, and give a reasonable amount of support for the children.' These two clauses were omitted." She claimed that the above witnesses were all Ye's friends. The court reviewed the testimony and, considering that witnesses needed to be summoned for questioning, announced a postponement for further hearing on December 30th. However, Ye also filed a counterclaim against Wu for defamation and false accusation, making the case very complex. Furthermore, Yang Zhuxia's complaint against Wu Yu for assault will continue to be heard this morning.

### Female Teacher Accuses School Principal, Case is Suspicious. Defendant Claims Both That It Never Happened and That There Was a Reconciliation. Plaintiff Has Never Appeared in Court Since Filing the Lawsuit.

Lin Jun, principal of Jingping Middle School at 552 Route du Père Robert, French Concession, from Pudong, was recently sued by Shen Fuzhen, a female teacher of English from Suzhou who left the school, in the Second Special District Court, Criminal Division, for offenses against public morals. After several court sessions and summons, the plaintiff has not yet been brought to court. The court discussed postponing the case, as reported in this newspaper. It has been reported that both the plaintiff and the defendant have made statements in the newspaper, saying that it never happened, and that the plaintiff filed a lawsuit in court, requesting to withdraw the lawsuit. The case was heard again yesterday by Presiding Judge Sun Pengxian in the Second Criminal Division, but the plaintiff, Shen Fuzhen, still did not report. Only the defendant's lawyer appeared and said, "The circumstances of this case are very peculiar. The plaintiff is not in court today. She published a newspaper on the 5th of this month saying she knew nothing about the case, but the plaintiff's statement had a lawyer, requesting a thorough investigation." The judge said, "This case could have been processed without a summons. The plaintiff has a withdrawal application that could end the case. Because the case is bizarre, it is being summoned again to clarify what happened. The plaintiff's statement was written by Lawyer You Zhi, and the withdrawal application seems to be two pieces of paper cut and pasted together. Furthermore, the defendant said it never happened, so why did he say there was a reconciliation? It can be seen that there are untruths on the defendant's side." The judge asked the defendant's lawyer, "Does the defendant know where the plaintiff is now?" The defendant's lawyer replied, "The defendant does not know her whereabouts because the plaintiff has been away from the school for a long time." He also presented a newspaper and said, "The plaintiff knew that today's hearing, and sent a letter to my lawyer." The court announced a postponement to 2:00 PM on the 30th for further hearing, and ordered the defendant to appear in court next time.

Liu Donghai Receives Threatening Letter with Bullet. County Public Security Bureau Has Ordered an Investigation.

A rural community report states that Liu Donghai, a resident of Huajing Town, Second District, Shanghai County, former head of the Caohang Township Administrative Bureau, a scholarly and literate man, has considerable savings. Donghai, nearly sixty years old, is still as energetic as a young man. Yesterday morning, Donghai found a Chinese-style envelope at the entrance to his house, addressed to "Mr. Liu Donghai." Upon opening it, he found a yellow slip of paper that read, "You have swallowed up the temple property, and I have no place to live. Please write out those 10,000 yuan, or else..." signed "Huajing Weilinggong." It also contained a bullet. Donghai, knowing it was a threatening letter, immediately took it to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau to report it. Patrol Officer Yang Hui examined the letter and questioned him, instructing Xia Hai to return home and wait quietly, while reporting the matter to the County Public Security Bureau. It is reported that the County Public Security Bureau has ordered its subordinates to investigate.

Accountants Association Holds Extraordinary General Meeting.

The Shanghai Accountants Association held an extraordinary general meeting yesterday at the Bankers Club. Over two hundred and forty members attended. The presidium consisted of Xi Yushu, Jiang Wanping, Wang Haifan, Xie Lin, and Bei Zuyi. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department, He Yuanming, and the Social Affairs Bureau, Zhang Dafu, attended the meeting. The meeting was conducted according to the agenda: (A) Report Items (omitted); (B) Discussion Items (1) Approval for the construction of the association's premises, increasing the budget for land, building, and equipment to 45,000 yuan, authorizing the Construction Committee to be responsible for the implementation; (2) Members Wang Yusheng et al. proposed regarding the levy of income tax, the Ministry's order for the Association to compile accounting systems for various industries, to formulate opinions, and requested a public vote. It was resolved to form an Income Tax Issues Research Committee, with an indefinite number of members, to be notified to the members by letter and convened by the Board of Directors; (3) The Municipal Party Department sent a letter, setting a date to convene various municipal agencies and organizations to discuss and organize the National Contribution of One Day's Income Movement Promotion Committee, hoping to nominate one important person in charge to attend on time. Resolved to delegate to the Board of Directors to designate a representative; (4) (Omitted); (5) (Omitted); (6) In accordance with the Association's charter, the election of officers was conducted. It was resolved that the terms of office for the nine directors and one vacancy, five supervisors, six alternate directors, and two alternate supervisors had expired. The full number of candidates should be submitted immediately, and tellers, vote counters, and recorders were designated. Voting began. As a result of the election, Xi Yushu, Li Hongshou, He Yuanming, Li Dawei, Jiang Wanping, Chen Xianmo, and six others were elected as directors. Xia Sunhuan, Qian Naicheng, Xu Yinghao, Qin Kai, Lu Yangchun, and five others were elected as supervisors. Wang Yusheng, Xu Pei, Zhao Zhenlong, Ye Danian, Sheng Yin, and Chen Luanqing, and six others were elected as alternate directors. Chen Zongshun and Dong Chunbiao, and two others were elected as alternate supervisors. (C) Temporary Motions (1) Members Feng Yixian, Xi Yushu, Jiang Wanping, Li Wenjie, Chen Xianmo, Pan Xulun, Wang Haifan, and others proposed that the bandit-puppet invasion in Suiyuan is a serious situation, and our frontline soldiers are making every effort to eliminate them. The whole country is in grief. In addition to sending a telegram of condolences, the Association should provide material assistance. It was resolved to allocate 1,000 yuan from the Construction Premises Fund for donations and to send letters to all members to actively donate. Donations should be sent to the Association for consolidation and transfer. Over 800 yuan were recognized for donation on the spot by the members, and those who did not donate will be notified by the Association; (2) Member Jiang Wanping proposed, seconded by Shen Xuejun, that during this extraordinary period of national crisis, in addition to the temporary assistance measures in the previous case, there should be long-term and steady response measures. It is proposed to uphold the spirit of perseverance and emulate the German and Italian methods of reducing food and expenses. All members should be notified to reduce daily expenses as much as possible. Entertainment and banquets should be greatly reduced, and even daily necessities should be used only from national products. On the one hand, the Association should open a special savings account for national salvation with state-owned financial institutions. All members or their relatives should send the money saved each month to the account for safekeeping, specially for national salvation needs. It was resolved to pass and instruct the Board of Directors to actively carry out; (3) Member Pan Xulun proposed, seconded by Wang Haifan, that according to the provisions of the Provisional Income Tax Regulations, the income of freelancers, whether calculated monthly or annually, should be paid according to half the monthly average. Furthermore, according to the provisions of the Implementation Rules of the Income Tax Law, in calculating the income of freelancers, business expenses should be deducted first, and the balance should be considered income and paid monthly. It is examined that the income of our accountants has a regular or continuous nature, but the monthly income varies greatly due to the quarterly relationship between the settlement of accounts and auditing of various institutions. As for business expenses, they should also be calculated together for a year and cannot be divided monthly. Therefore, in calculating income, the correct amount of monthly average income can only be obtained by deducting the total annual expenses from the total annual income. Therefore, it is really difficult to comply with the monthly declaration and payment of income tax. It is proposed that a telegram be sent to the Ministry of Finance in the name of the entire meeting of over two hundred and forty members of the general assembly today, requesting that the implementation rules of the income tax be modified to change the reporting of the income of freelancers to be done within three months after the annual settlement, and to change the payment of income tax of freelancers to "within a certain number of days after the annual settlement declaration" in order to ensure the accuracy of the calculation of average income. This is our duty, and we respectfully request a public vote. It was resolved to pass and instruct the Board of Directors to handle it expeditiously. (Rest omitted)

Record of the Physicians Association Autumn General Meeting.

The city's Physicians Association held its autumn general meeting yesterday at 5 p.m. at Yipinxiang, with over two hundred members attending, including Xu Naili, as well as representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Mao Yun, the Health Bureau, Tao Ji'an, legal counsel Qu Yue, and accounting counsel Wang Wannian. The meeting was presided over by Xu Naili, and the meeting opened with ceremonial procedures. First, the chairman reported on association affairs, and the various special committee members reported on past work. Next, representatives Mao from the Municipal Party Department and Tao from the Health Bureau, as well as the various counselors, gave speeches (speeches omitted for length). Then, the chairman gave a thank-you speech and welcomed the new members. Then they immediately discussed important proposals: (1) Wang Qizhang proposed that the Association should purchase premises as soon as possible (resolved to pass); (2) Cai Yumen proposed that the health authorities should strictly ban the impersonation of physicians to protect lives (resolved to pass); (3) Chen Heng proposed that various medical certificates should be drafted and issued to all members, in a uniform format to emphasize professionalism (resolved to pass), that the Association should recommend to the National Physicians Federation to submit a request to the Central Government to issue various diagnostic certificate formats; (4) Chu Buqiu proposed that the health authorities should prohibit the use of new drugs by traditional Chinese medicine practitioners by law, reiterating the ban to value the lives of the people (resolved to pass in principle, to be carefully drafted by the next Executive Committee); (5) Ye Zhisheng and Wang Wanbai proposed that the situation in Suiyuan is urgent, and donations should be raised immediately, medicines and anti-gas materials should be collected, and transported to the front lines to actively participate in aid (resolved to pass in principle, to be handled by the Executive Committee); (7) Fan Shouyuan proposed that the Association should organize a poison gas protection committee as soon as possible to instill poison gas protection knowledge to the public and promote poison gas protection facilities in the city (resolved to pass); (8) Wang Wanbai proposed that the hygiene knowledge drafts issued by the Central Government to various radio stations should be broadcast by physicians (resolved to pass to the next Executive Committee for further discussion). After the discussion, the officers were re-elected. As a result, Xu Naili, Zhu Yanggao, Jin Wenhong, You Pengxi, Wu Yichu, Pang Jingzhou, Yu Songjun, Kong Xipeng, Zhou Junchang, Huang Zhong, Ye Zhisheng, Xia Shenchu, Song Guobin, and Chen Rongzhang were elected as executive committee members. Jiang Zhenxun, Zhang Zidao, Ding Huikang, and Zhu Kewen were elected as alternate executive committee members. Wang Qizhang, Cai Yumen, Yu Yunxiu, Guo Qiyuan, and Yang Yuanji were elected as supervisors. Shen Chengwu and Xie Junshou were elected as alternate supervisors. After the meeting, there was a dinner, and the meeting adjourned.

City Federation Petitions for Prohibition of Using Confucius as a Trademark

The Shanghai First Special District Citizen's Federation, because it found that the Feng Baoji firm at 210 Jiujiang Road, Public Concession, sells imported "Little Luzon" cigars, with Confucius as a trademark, and publishes in newspapers, advertising widely, believes that Confucius is a master teacher of our country's past dynasties, established the foundation of rites and righteousness, laid the foundation of the country, and, like Sun Yat-sen's founding of the Republic, benefited all people. All Chinese people should respect him. How can they be desecrated at will? Furthermore, respect for Confucius has long been ordered to be followed. Now, taking it as a trademark for consumable goods like cigars is a deliberate desecration. Based on the above two points, the federation specially petitions the Ministry of Industry, asking whether to consult the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the Little Luzon authorities to cancel or prohibit its domestic sales, and to issue a general ban, prohibiting the use of Confucius as a trademark for any kind of goods in the future, in order to comply with the government's order to respect Confucius and to show the public's respect for sages.

North Xizang Road Retains Original Road Name

The Shanghai Municipal Council had previously decided that after Xizang Road was renamed Yu Qiaqing Road, the North Xizang Road section would also have its "North" removed and be called Xizang Road, etc. It is now learned that the Shanghai Municipal Council has recently changed its original decision and canceled the resolution of July 22 of this year. In the future, North Xizang Road will retain its original name and will not be renamed. The reason is that all streets running west from the Bund to the Suzhou Creek have the same name, with the "North" character appended to the section north of the Suzhou Creek. Now that Xizang Road has been renamed Yu Qiaqing Road, if the northern section must be renamed, it should be renamed "North Yu Qiaqing Road." However, since North Xizang Road is a road name already familiar to the citizens, and the postal and telecommunications services have also become accustomed to it, any changes would likely cause misunderstandings.

Police Chief Shen Zhenhua Strictly Investigates Opium Smokers

Shen Zhenhua, chief of the Lao Beimen Police Station, has been diligently carrying out the work of conducting anti-drug propaganda and investigating opium smokers. Recently, as the deadline for the third phase of opium smokers' license renewal is approaching, he has intensified his work. Yesterday, he led officers to search the Wanmu Di area and found over fifty unlicensed opium smokers and those who voluntarily surrendered themselves for rehabilitation. All were taken to the station for questioning and transferred to the General Bureau for disposition. Also, Patrol Officer Hu Chongmin found Xu Shiquan operating an opium den under the guise of a license at 35 Gaodun Road and seized three pauper's licenses that no one claimed. He took them to the station to be sent to the Bureau.

Page 12

Increase in Rickshaw License Fees, Request for Change in Handling

The Social Affairs Bureau is organizing literacy schools, and the rickshaw association of the special district, due to the increase in rickshaw license fees by the municipal council, has written to the director general requesting that he withdraw the order. Details are as follows:

Request for Guarantee The Public Concession Shanghai Municipal Council announced that, starting on January 1, the public rickshaw license fee would be increased by 1.50 yuan per month, and the mutual aid society fee would be abolished. The rickshaw association has written to the director general for a guarantee, the original text of which reads: "To the esteemed Director General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, we respectfully submit that we have examined the recent regulations issued by the Shanghai Municipal Council, to be implemented from January 1, 1937, increasing the rickshaw license fee by 1.50 yuan per month, to be used as a mutual aid fund. The understanding of our members is that the income from this increased vehicle tax should be entirely allocated by the Shanghai Municipal Council to subsidize the mutual aid society. If the Shanghai Municipal Council stops this subsidy for any reason in the future, the increased vehicle tax should be immediately stopped from being collected. We hope that Your Excellency will grant a guarantee for the views expressed by our members, and we would be grateful."

Letter to Fei Xindun At the same time, the association wrote to Director Fei Xindun, stating: "We respectfully submit that we have read the announcement No. 4758 of your bureau on October 23, which states that the public rickshaw license fee will be set at 3.50 yuan in national currency per vehicle from January 1, 1937, etc. It is known that public rickshaws in the Public Concession pay a monthly license fee of two yuan to the Shanghai Municipal Council, two yuan to the French Municipal Council, and one yuan to the Municipal Government. If the Public Concession Shanghai Municipal Council suddenly increases the public rickshaw license fee to 3.50 yuan, the French Municipal Council and the Municipal Government will inevitably increase it as well, making it unbearable for the rickshaw merchants. On the same day, the public announcement also interpreted that the increased license fee would enable the Shanghai Municipal Council to allocate the increased vehicle tax to subsidize the expenses of the mutual aid society. The association believes that the recent regulations made by the Shanghai Municipal Council have an apparent suspicion of discriminating against and assisting laborers in the concession, so whether this regulation is legal is highly questionable. If the Shanghai Municipal Council really wants to collect the mutual aid fee according to the new system, the association believes that this goal can be achieved through another route, making it equally satisfactory without any illegality. The association is also willing to prepay the 1.50 yuan mutual aid fee per vehicle per month for each rickshaw merchant and collect it from each rickshaw merchant and issue receipts, so that each rickshaw merchant can present the receipts when applying for a license each month, so that the vehicle license will still be two yuan per month, and the clear name of the increased tax can be avoided, and the actions of the Shanghai Municipal Council will not have legal problems. We respectfully report this to you and hope you will consider it with sympathy and reply accordingly."

Calling for Assistance The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in order to promote literacy education for laborers, recently advocated running rickshaw driver literacy schools, stipulating that each vehicle would pay 0.30 yuan per month. Preparations have already begun and the rickshaw association has been notified to inform all members to comply. The rickshaw merchants have expressed their full agreement with this, but because they are afraid that the increase in license fees by the Shanghai Municipal Council will be followed by simultaneous increases by the French Concession and the Public Concession, it would be truly unbearable in this time of economic hardship. Therefore, they have asked various circles to negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council to withdraw the increase in fees. The Public Concession issued certificates to the rickshaw owners, stipulating that starting on the first of next month, a handling fee of 0.20 yuan and a deposit of 1 yuan would be collected per vehicle. Yesterday, it issued Instruction No. 3629 to the association ordering them to inform the rickshaw merchants to comply.

Employees of Silk Factories in Zhabei Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday, Requesting That the Factories Be Ordered to Pay Off Back Wages

The Yuanxing and Yuanji silk reeling factories on Hutai Road in Zhabei recently announced a shutdown starting on the 29th of last month due to a shortage of raw materials and insufficient reeling. However, since the two factories started operations in May of this year, the wages of their employees have not been fully paid. The workers have found that the factories had considerable profits last year and are now deliberately making excuses, ignoring the workers' livelihoods. They have separately presented the matter to the Party and government authorities, requesting assistance. The Social Affairs Bureau convened two mediations, but no resolution has been reached due to differing opinions between the two parties. The workers have been unemployed for a long time, and as the weather is getting colder, it is difficult to maintain their livelihoods if this continues to be unresolved. Therefore, at 10 a.m. yesterday, over forty workers gathered and walked to the city center to petition the Municipal Government. However, they were stopped from advancing near the Public Security Bureau due to the large number of people. The workers then nominated Tang Shaoxiong, Hua Gendi, Cai Jisheng, Lu Huaisan, and Li Acai, and six others, as representatives to submit a petition to the Municipal Government. Zhang Shiwu from the Second Section of the Administration received them, inquired about the situation, and promised to order the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate immediately. They then went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, where Wang Xianqing from the Third Section received them, stating that the dispute had been reported to the Director for review, and asked the workers to wait quietly for a resolution. The workers dispersed around 1 p.m.

Fishery Loan Syndicate Making Efforts to Investigate, Loans to be Released in Spring Fishing Season, 120,000 Already Loaned Out by Three Banks

The Fishery Loan Syndicate, organized by the Ministry of Industry in conjunction with China, Communications, and twelve other banks, appointed Qian Xinzhi, Wang Zhihua, and Gui Yanfang as preparatory committee members, and established a preparatory office, starting operations at the Xinhua Bank. All three drafts of the organizational regulations, operating rules, and work outline have been approved by the two preparatory meetings and submitted to the Ministry for record. It is reported that the total amount of the syndicate's funds is one million yuan. 200,000 of which will be undertaken by the Ministry, has been written to the Ministry of Finance. The remaining 800,000 yuan has been prepared by the participating banks according to the amount they have determined to pay. Regarding the syndicate's business policy, the general rules for the organization of various fishery production and marketing cooperatives, the investigation of fishery conditions, and the current status of fishery cooperatives, the preparatory office has dispatched personnel to carry out these tasks separately and has scheduled a third preparatory meeting this week to discuss further progress. The date of its official establishment will be determined after the completion of various investigation tasks. However, in order to relieve the fishermen, the loans will be started no later than the spring fishing season next year. Up to 120,000 yuan have been jointly loaned out by the Zhonghui and Xinhua and the Four Banks Savings Association. Now that the winter fishing season has arrived, applications are pouring in and all the loans will soon be loaned out.

After the Party and National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau was ordered to cease operations, the Bureau relayed the order to the branch bureaus in various provinces to comply. The directors of the branch bureaus believed that the branch sales offices in the counties under their jurisdiction had a large number of flags in stock, and that complying with the order to close required all matters such as the remaining flags to be resolved first. They had sent letters and telegrams to the Bureau requesting instructions, but the Bureau replied that it had already requested instructions from the Central Government and would notify them as soon as the approval was received. Because it had been a long time and no approval had been received, the directors of the various branch bureaus had come to Shanghai one after another. Yesterday, they went to the Bureau to appeal for the resolution of the remaining matters and the return of the flag prices. Further Capture of Bandit Accomplices

The Wang family residing at No. 2 Hongfu Lane, Fangbang Road, Nanshi, was burgled on October 27th last year, with valuables worth over 1,000 yuan stolen. Recently, the Municipal Police Bureau arrested five bandits including Xu Fusheng, who confessed that their accomplice, Song Laisheng, had committed other burglaries in the concession. He was handed over to the First Special District Court for trial, sentenced to eight years and two months imprisonment, and is currently serving his sentence.

The other day, the Municipal Police Bureau transferred him for further questioning. According to his statement, another accomplice, a Ningbo native named Wang Fengchun, provided firearms, and Li A’ming acted as a lookout. Wang resided at No. 17 Yuanfang Road, and Li lived at No. 60 Mike Road. Detective Zhu Lie of the Criminal Investigation Team then contacted the Hongkou and Zhabei police stations, requesting their assistance in the arrest. Chinese detectives Yang Xinzheng, Zhang Desheng, and detective Chen Jinsheng were dispatched to arrest Wang and Li at their respective addresses. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court.

Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department stated that the two defendants denied the charges at the police station and requested that they be temporarily detained pending a public summons from the Shanghai Local Court. According to Song Laisheng, the Fangbang Road Hongfu Lane robbery involved eight people, including Wang, Li, and the five arrested bandits including Xu Fusheng. Afterward, Wang received 50 yuan and a gold ring, and Li also received 50 yuan and a watch. The two defendants claimed that this was a false accusation due to previous gambling disputes. Judge Xiao ordered them to be remanded in custody for further hearing this Friday.

Mischievous Child Climbs Onto Back of Truck, Falls and Gets Injured When Truck Starts

A cargo truck, No. 12208 from the Shanghai Municipal Council’s South Shanghai Engineering Department, was being driven by driver Jiang A’rong. At 5 PM yesterday, while passing the Old West Gate, the truck stopped at a red light. Unexpectedly, three mischievous children from the neighborhood took the opportunity to climb onto the back of the truck to play. When the light turned green and the truck moved forward, the other two mischievous children jumped off the back of the truck, but one child named Jiang Xiaomao fell and was seriously injured, unable to move. A police officer on duty witnessed the incident and took the injured child to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. His injuries were severe.

The driver was taken to the West Gate Branch Bureau for questioning and it was determined that the driver was not at fault. The mischievous child’s parents were to blame for their lack of discipline. The Public Works Department released Jiang on bail.

Dr. Chen Bangdian Moves Clinic; Specializes in Reproductive Urology and Offers Injection Therapy for Smoking Cessation

Dr. Chen Bangdian, an American-trained Master of Urology and Doctor of Medicine, has recently moved his clinic to the Wuzhou Pharmacy Building on Hankou Road due to the growth of his practice and the inadequacy of his original clinic. Dr. Chen is currently a professor at the Women's Medical College and a physician at Renji Hospital and Juyi Hospital. He specializes in the treatment of reproductive and urinary diseases. For smoking cessation, he has formulated a special injection drug that counteracts opium, which causes an aversion to tobacco upon injection, gradually reducing the amount of smoking without any pain. Many people have quit smoking using this method. Free trials are available. Detailed information can be obtained by writing to the clinic.

Lawyer Zhou Guoying Moves His Office

Lawyer Zhou Guoying has been practicing law in Shanghai for many years. He is known for his careful study and accurate interpretation of the law in all cases entrusted to him by various sectors of society. He was previously located at No. 25 Dade Lane, Gordon Road. However, this location was too remote and not close to the various courts in the city. Clients also found it inconvenient to travel to and discuss their cases. Therefore, at the request of various sectors of society, Lawyer Zhou has chosen a new location for his office at No. 6 Tianlu Lane, No. 120, North Zhejiang Road, near the First Special District Court. He moved to the new office on the 19th of this month and will continue to practice law as usual.

Qin Niu Farm Continues to Welcome Visitors

The Fenghua Qin Niu Agricultural and Forestry Farm, founded in the first year of the Republic of China, is holding a 25th-anniversary celebration from October 1st to 30th. Industrial enthusiasts are welcome to visit the farm for guidance. The farm's Shanghai office at No. 27 Songshan Road, French Concession, is responsible for receiving visitors and distributing visitor passes. Although the deadline has passed for many days, many industrial enthusiasts have continued to request tickets and purchase seedlings from the branch office, and still want to visit the farm, with dozens of requests every day. To accommodate this enthusiasm, the farm has requested instructions from the headquarters, which has approved an extension of one month until the end of next month. Horticulture enthusiasts should not miss this opportunity.

"Science" Magazine, Issue 11 is Published

"Science" Magazine, Volume 20, Issue 11, published by the Science Society of China, has been released. This issue contains articles, including "Personal Views on Scientific Papers" by Yuan Hanqing, "Observations of the Solar Eclipse in Hokkaido" by Yu Qingsong and Chen Zunjiao, "Report on Observations of the Solar Eclipse in Siberia" by Li Heng and Zhang Yuzhe, "Properties of Wood in Water" by Xu Zhenru, "Food and Nutrition" by Hou Xiangchuan, "Geomagnetism and Geology" by Ding Yi, and "Wanderer Layers" by Li Xiaofang. These articles are written by experts and introduce new theories, or offer original insights and contributions to science. The report on the observation of the solar eclipse is a particularly timely and important work that should not be missed. In addition, there are forty-four scientific news items, covering rare and interesting events in the scientific community both at home and abroad, which are most welcomed by scholars. The price for this issue is 25 cents in national currency. It is sold by the Publication Management Department of the Science Society of China at No. 533 Ya Wu Road, Shanghai, and is also available at the China Science Company at No. 649 Foch Road and the Shanghai Magazine Company at No. 4 Sima Road. Furthermore, Issue 10 of "Science," which is a special issue for the General Assembly of Seven Scientific Organizations in Beiping, has been selling very well since its publication. There are few copies left, so those who wish to purchase it should do so quickly.
