Shanghai's Enamel Industry (Continued) (An Overview of Shanghai Industries - No. 38)

— Compiled by China Credit Information Service

1. Huafeng Enamel Co., Ltd. – The factory was established in 1928, funded by Liu Hongsheng and others, with a registered capital of 300,000 yuan, increased by 8,900 yuan. The current chairman of the board is Mr. Li Bake, the managing director is Mr. Ji Zhishi, and the assistant manager is Mr. Hu Linsheng. The factory is located in Zhoujiabo, Pudong, and the sales office is located on Laobeimen Street. In the past, it formed a joint sales office with Zhufeng and other factories on Avenue Edward VII to eliminate competition, but this has now expired. The base of the factory in Pudong is worth approximately 123,000 yuan, the machinery in the factory is worth approximately 120,000 yuan, the 24 furnaces are worth approximately 35,600 yuan, and other various models are worth over 20,000 yuan. The factory's main product is washbasins, with the "Ruyi" brand trademark. The turnover has increased year by year, and in recent years it has reached about 1 million yuan per year. As for operating profits and losses, they often fluctuate due to the influence of the situation and competition. Last year, there was a loss of 25,268.18 yuan. This year's business is estimated to be slightly profitable.

2. Yifeng Enamel Factory Co., Ltd. – The factory was founded in August 1920. It was reorganized from the Guangda Factory by Mr. Dong Jifu of Wu County. Initially, it only produced rice bowls, food baskets, mouthwash cups, etc., but now it also manufactures ceramic tiles and modern porcelain, using the "Money" brand trademark. The total capital is 350,000 yuan. The factory has a total of five factories. The addresses are as follows: the main factory is located on Jumen Road in Nanshi, the second factory is located on Dapulu Railway South, the third factory is located on Rihui East Road in Rihuigang, the fourth factory is located in Chenjiaqiao, South Railway Station, and the fifth factory is located in Fangcun, Guangzhou. The general sales office is located on Avenue Edward VII. The factory was the first to manufacture enamel powder, saving profits and recovering rights, which is commendable. The current second board of directors includes Wang Yousong, Rong Fangzhou, Dong Jifu, Dong Boying, Xie Xiangming, and Li Weiliang. Zhang Fengshou, Zhu Rangcheng, and Zhu Xianhuai are the supervisors of the factory. The factory has the best business, reaching over one million yuan annually, and has annual profits. According to the board of directors' report, last year's turnover reached over 1.2 million yuan, with a net profit of over 40,000 yuan.

Chronicles

Tidbits

— (Tai Xuan)

The three stages of life can be compared to crossing a bridge: youth is like ascending the bridge, middle age is like crossing the bridge, and old age is like descending the bridge.

These few words may seem like platitudes at first glance, but if you savor them carefully, they contain profound meaning. When ascending the bridge, you must take each step steadily and without haste, to avoid stumbling. Similarly, during the period of youth, one should concentrate on studying, progressing gradually until completing one's studies. This is the first stage of life, the first stage of ascending the bridge.

Once on the bridge, the path is relatively smooth. Middle age is like applying one's knowledge, unleashing one's full potential to accomplish life's most important tasks. This is the second stage of life, the second stage of crossing the bridge.

Watching the elderly slowly descend the bridge step by step undoubtedly signifies their declining energy, requiring rest and enjoyment. This work of descending the bridge is, of course, the final stage of life. Bridges, whether east, west, north, or south, can be crossed back and forth, but can people return to their youth? The ancients said, "If you don't work hard when you're young, you'll regret it when you're old." This is a good warning for young people.

Spy Jokes in Tokyo

— Bili

Modern cities are battlegrounds for spies to compete and win. Some use ingenious disguises, some use secret communications, and some use the dimples of beautiful women. People from friendly countries are famous for going to various countries to spy on various secrets, and at the same time, there are many foreign spies active in Tokyo. Therefore, the work of the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department is always tense.

One day, a woman named Osawa came to the police station, looking very flustered. She reported to the police chief: "My husband, Nagami, has been acting suspiciously lately, and his whereabouts are erratic. He often receives letters from Moscow, which he locks away very secretly. I suspect that he is a Russian spy because I love my country, so I came to report it. A week ago, he received a letter from Vladivostok and hurried out, and has not returned since. I am afraid there is a major incident, so please pay attention to the investigation."

The police station immediately became tense after receiving this report. They first quietly sent detectives to search Osawa's home. After a thorough inspection, nothing suspicious was found except for a large pile of letters from Moscow in the safe. Nagami runs a leather goods shop, and his accounts showed that he was heavily in debt. The letters from Moscow were just ordinary talk about leather goods transactions, but the police station thought they were worth studying and took them back for investigation. The police station also inquired with police stations and customs offices in various places, but there was no record of anyone named Nagami leaving the country. The more they investigated, the more confused they became, and the more confused they became, the more serious the case seemed. After four or five days of this, Nagami was finally found. The spy ringleader was arrested. Nagami was found by police officers in a forest on the outskirts of Tokyo, looking like neither a human nor a ghost. When he was arrested, his wife Osawa rushed to the police station, and the truth of the case was revealed. Osawa said: "My husband is really not a spy. Lately, he has been depressed because his business has failed and he is heavily in debt. He disappeared a week ago, and I was very anxious and could not find him, so I fabricated the story that he was a spy and reported it to the police station, asking the police officers to put in extra effort to find this person. Now, thank you for finding him."

The great spy case came to an end.

How to Wear a Hat?

— Xu Jichen

There is a psychology professor at a university in Bolivia, South America, named Alina. She says, "I have always adhered to a principle as my standard for choosing a partner: how does that man wear his hat? Some men like to wear their hats to the side, some tilt them to the right, covering their ears. This is a sign of cunning and fickleness. These people are generally unreliable. There are also people who wear their hats over their eyes, almost covering them completely. These people will never take risks in their lives. They are very timid and can never accomplish great things. Just imagine, can a man who is more timid than a woman be called a husband? There are also those who wear their hats very far back, exposing their faces and foreheads completely. These people are reckless. If you marry such a person, you must prepare to be a widow, or remarry. A man must wear his hat squarely, without leaning to the left or right, or tilting forward or backward. This is our standard for women to choose a partner."

Undoubtedly, when we go out to the streets and see many men wearing felt hats, they are always styled in a three-seven split, with a greasy look. Or they wear their hats on top of their heads, covering even the back of their heads. Most of the hooligans who stick out their thumbs and roll up their sleeves are like this. Calling them "reckless" is certainly very appropriate. Wearing a hat squarely, and following the rules in every move, is naturally a sign of a "formal person." As for those who wear their hats askew, or hats covering their eyelids, these people are probably young, and when they see women on the road, whether it's one or two, their glistening eyes will shoot out a flame from the edge of their hats; of course, they are fickle and not people you can rely on for life! Some people even wear melon-skin caps, also tilted to one side. These people are either ushers in theaters, or leisurely people carrying birdcages, or the bosses of bookstores, or even the people who live off the mountains and rivers!

Ms. Alina's theory above is very helpful to us. Although we can't say that a man's way of wearing a hat is the golden rule for choosing a partner, sometimes we find it very effective.

Ladies, ladies who seek happiness, whether or not your partner is suitable is tied to your lifelong joys and sorrows. If you want to hunt down a passionate and righteous partner, the first step should be to take Alina's words as your motto.

This is a philosophy of wearing a hat, and also an art of wearing a hat. Brothers and sisters, go and savor it carefully.

Guides

— Wang Yu

The guides referred to here are not the kind that use women's sex appeal as an enticement like the common variants of prostitution. These guides are formally engaged in guiding work, and their only customers are passengers on ocean liners passing through Shanghai.

They have no organization and go to the customs baggage inspection area or the docks where huge ships are docked to find customers on their own. Dressed in beautiful suits, when they walk on the deck and hear someone saying, "Shanghai is a good place," they will politely approach them and say in fluent English:

"Sir, I am a guide in Shanghai. Would you like me to take you sightseeing?"

Naturally, these passengers will be suspicious of these unfamiliar Chinese people, especially since they have heard that there are many swindlers in Shanghai! So he will tell the passengers: all the expenses on shore (such as taxi fares) will be paid by him, until you have finished your tour to your satisfaction, and then you will repay him the amount, and in addition, give him some "tips" at will.

After receiving a customer, they usually go out by car, but the guide is unwilling to spend three yuan an hour on taxi fares to make money for the taxi company. He has already contacted those black-plate unlicensed taxis parked on the docks, and the fares are naturally cheaper, but he still reports three yuan per hour to the guest, just because he can profit from it. (To be continued)

Three Renunciations

— Zhou Xian

This is a true story from my hometown. The protagonist is the fourth daughter of a former county magistrate. From a young age, the fourth daughter was betrothed under her parents' orders. Unfortunately, ten years ago, when she was seventeen, her fiancé died of illness. She was deeply affected by this and further influenced by traditional moral teachings. She cried and demanded to live a life of chastity. Her parents strongly opposed this, so she went on a hunger strike to coerce them. After persuasion from relatives and friends, she compromised and entered a Buddhist nunnery. Her parents allowed her to practice her faith with her hair intact, but she insisted on shaving her head, again using a hunger strike as leverage. Her parents couldn't resist her, so they had to let her shave her head and take the Buddhist name Lianyin.

The fourth daughter's decision to become a nun was merely a momentary impulse. After shaving her head, the morning bells and evening drums, vegetarian meals, and meditation created a life of sorrow and loneliness that she naturally couldn't endure. However, she stubbornly kept up appearances but suffered in her heart. Whenever her mother came to visit, her face would be covered in tears and snot. Her mother understood her daughter's psychology, so she often provoked her with words. The old nuns were especially perceptive when dealing with the wives and daughters of gentlemen's families and tried to encourage her. After a year, the fourth daughter returned to secular life, grew her hair back, and sought a new match.

At the age of twenty, the fourth daughter married a newly widowed elementary school principal introduced by her cousin. The wedding was scheduled for February, but unexpectedly, the elementary school principal died of illness. The fourth daughter cried for two nights in a fit of anger. Taking advantage of a moment when no one was watching, she cut off her black hair again and secretly returned to the nunnery where she had originally practiced. However, her mother couldn't bear to let her daughter become a nun, so she asked many relatives to persuade her to return home and find another suitable match. The fourth daughter was adamant in her refusal. After much persuasion, they finally agreed to send her to Shanghai to study, to seek independence and no longer mention marriage.

Once in Shanghai, she lived in the school dormitory, studied diligently, and made rapid progress. She gradually forgot her past pain. Later, she gradually developed a romantic relationship with a classmate's brother, starting from friendship. Three years ago, when she was twenty-five, she officially married. I even went to congratulate her on her wedding. They were a perfect couple, and their love was excellent after the wedding. Last year, they had a daughter. Unexpectedly, their beloved daughter died young this spring, and in the autumn, her husband died of typhoid fever. This shock was naturally even deeper than the previous two. Therefore, she followed her parents-in-law's advice and returned to her mother's home temporarily to mourn.

But I received news yesterday that she had attempted suicide and was rescued. Recently, she shaved her head again and devoted herself to a Buddhist temple.

The Phoenix Replaces the Oriole

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Vows Made with a Cup of Water, Talking of Woe Under the Green Lamp; Golden Rings and Red Beans Convey Yearning

Menglan heard this and exclaimed "Ah ya!" expressing surprise. Youmei said, "Ah ya what? I don't think this is outside the realm of human emotions." Menglan said, "It's nothing to send a friend a gift or two. But a gold ring like this shouldn't be given to just anyone." Youhai said, "Of course, in my opinion, it can't be seen as a casual act on your part. If you feel this ring isn't appropriate to give, I'm just delivering a gift for someone else, so of course I can't force you." Saying this, she put the ring on the table. Menglan supported her right hand with her left, looking at the ring finger on her left hand where she used to wear a ring. She frowned slightly, smiled, and slowly said, "If we get along well with each other, it's not excessive to give a ring. But if our friendship is limited to letters, that's too superficial. How could I give him something I wear myself?" Youmei laughed, "If that's the case, I'm trying to teach a master craftsman. I've heard two stories before. One person could play the zither, and another person understood it. Later, when that person died, he burned the zither. Another person was wearing a sword, and a friend saw it and wanted it. But he was under orders from the emperor, so he gave it to his friend. Later, when his official business was done, his friend had died, so he hung the sword on the tree by his grave." Menglan laughed, "That person, that person, you said seven or eight of them, I can't keep it straight." Youmei laughed, "When you hear me say this, please forgive me. I don't have any historical allusions in my head, I can't help but say it. Can you learn from the ancients?" Menglan laughed, "It's just that your two metaphors aren't very auspicious." Youmei said, "That's right. The ancients didn't give away the sword at the time, so the omen wasn't good. If you give it away immediately, you won't have the same bad outcome as the ancients." Menglan still looked down at her finger. She pondered for a long, long time before saying, "Since that's the case, then take it." (101)

Whereabouts

Visiting the Osmanthus at Zhu Nunnery

— Xian Xian

Zhu Nunnery is located southeast of Jiaxing County, less than ten li from the county seat. The location is remote and the site is small, not as magnificent and grand as the Lingyan and Lenyen temples in the city. However, the nunnery has two osmanthus trees that are hundreds of years old. During the Qing Dynasty's Xianfeng and Tongzhi reigns, the county suffered from war. The sweet pear trees that shaded the duke of Shao's court and the tall trees of noble families were destroyed and damaged, and few survived. The osmanthus trees of the nunnery were preserved because they were located in a remote village, escaping the axes of woodcutters. As the years passed, their presence became increasingly majestic and beautiful. The nunnery is famous for its osmanthus trees, making it one of the famous scenic spots in the county. On the twenty-third day of the ninth month of the Bingzi year, the osmanthus trees were in full bloom, and the autumn light was clear and bright. Suddenly moved by the pleasant scenery, I took a walk to visit them alone. Leaving the old site of the south gate, I walked south along the side of the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway. After crossing three bridges, I went down the railway and walked southeast until I reached a body of water with a stone beam spanning it from east to west, called Jiangshui Bridge. Crossing the bridge and walking southeast, after several turns, I looked north at a small nunnery with red walls by the roadside, named Zhiyuan She Nunnery. The locals simply call it She Nunnery, pronouncing "she" as "shai". After passing She Nunnery, I continued southeast. Looking east by the roadside, there was a village with lush forests and houses, called Xuejia Du. Arriving here, I didn't know how far I was from Zhu Nunnery, so I entered the village to find someone to ask. The creek was damp and meandered around the village. Looking around, all the doors were closed, and there was no trace of anyone. It must have been because the harvest of rice had not yet begun, and everyone was busy harvesting. The men and women of the village were all in the fields. While wandering around, I looked across the creek and saw two or three village children playing by the water. I hurried to their location to ask them. As I approached, they saw a stranger and scattered in all directions like startled wild geese or frightened deer, running through the forests and streams. I shouted loudly, and two dogs under the eaves, fierce as tigers and leopards, were startled by the sound and barked madly. The owner of the dogs heard the noise and came out, shouting at them. The two dogs then lowered their ears and wagged their tails, leaving. I asked about the location of Zhu Nunnery, and they pointed to the roof tiles vaguely visible among the evergreen pine and cypress trees in the southeast, saying, "That's it." Calmed down and regained my composure, I followed their directions. After a short while, I arrived at a stone bridge called Zhuanghou Bridge. The stream was like a ribbon, clear to the bottom. Climbing the bridge and looking southeast, I saw a structure by the river a few dozen feet away, with sparse trees. This was Zhu Nunnery. The ancient fragrance of osmanthus had already arrived with the wind, strong and refreshing. I went down the bridge and entered the nunnery, which occupied a small area surrounded by white walls. In the courtyard were two osmanthus trees, arranged on the left and right. My feet were tired from walking for a long time, so I rested under the trees, focusing on observing them. I saw old trunks and gnarled branches extending in all directions, winding like dragons and snakes, and curling like arms and legs. The moss was mottled, and their ancient strangeness was hard to describe. Ropes and cables were tied around them, each tree divided into five platforms, arranged in an orderly manner, with the height not overlapping. The green leaves were luxuriant, and the golden flowers were scattered. As the flowers were blooming, I remembered visiting the nunnery with my late mother when I was a child while visiting family graves. At that time, the nunnery had an old neighbor, who was sixty or seventy years old, who explained that the osmanthus trees were originally two, one on the left, whose age was unknown, and one on the right, which had withered in its old age. He had personally seen it replanted when he was young, so its trunk was smaller. According to the old man, the age of the tree on the right was about the same as his own. Now, another fifty years have passed, so the tree on the left is also over a hundred years old. The children like me who used to play bamboo games are now getting old, not far from the age of the old man. Recalling the past, I felt lost. Therefore, I composed a seven-character quatrain: "I once visited the Buddhist palace with my mother, recognizing the snow geese that were the previous life of the golden millet. For fifty years, nothing has happened. The double osmanthus trees of Zhu Nunnery are in the autumn wind again." After finishing the poem, I recited it several times, unable to overcome the feeling of wasting my life. The nunnery used to have nuns, but now there is only one old woman who serves the incense. When guests arrive, she cooks tea and offers refreshments, fulfilling the duties of a hostess. I then paid my respects to the Buddha statue, looked around the hall, and lingered for a long time before leaving the nunnery. Passing Zhuanghou Bridge, I saw an ancient tomb on the east side of the bridge, with a magnificent layout and lush pine and cypress trees. Among the scattered weeds, a stone tablet stood tall. I read it and it was titled "Double Osmanthus Hall". How strange, the theory of geography, half of the world believes it, such a coincidence, there is probably heaven in it. According to old legends, the site of the nunnery belongs to the southeast corner of the county seat. Going southeast from the nunnery, there is Zhutian Village, the former residence of Zhang Shuwei Tingji. Mr. Zhang was famous throughout the country for his learning, and his father and son both led the Zhejiang provincial examinations, but neither was able to become a Jinshi. The story of osmanthus trees is originally a sign of academic success. The flowers bloom in the autumn, so they only indicate success in the provincial examinations. The double osmanthus trees must also be the response of Zhang Minqiao's clan. The old rumors are like this, so the descendants of the so-called Double Osmanthus Hall probably also benefited from the shade of the osmanthus trees of the nunnery, and once occupied a high position in the court at that time? I don't know. Walking, walking, and walking again, I followed the old road home. By the time I arrived home, it was noon.

Sports News

The Last Game of the First Round of the Tung Wah League: Tung Wah vs. French Club on Saturday at Recreation Ground; The Victory or Defeat Concerns the Championship of Group A; Kwong Nan vs. Portuguese on Sunday at Hongkou Park

The most important match of the Western League soccer this weekend is Tung Wah vs. French Club, held on Saturday at Recreation Ground. This is the last game of Tung Wah's first round. In the past results, Tung Wah has seven wins and one draw, while French Club has six wins and one draw. Since they still have one game against Shaheir, French Club will definitely win.

The results of this year's Group A are still not out of the pattern of the previous two years, with Tung Wah and French Club competing for the championship. This has become an inevitable fact. Looking at the French Club's lineup, it is stronger than when they won the championship in the previous two years. This is because their talents are average, and they are brave and good at fighting. Tung Wah is the elite of the Chinese people, with concentrated talent, and their soccer skills have reached perfection. It is a pity that their stamina is not as good as French Club, which is a concern for all soccer fans. Based on the last performance match for birthday congratulations and the game against Rucks yesterday, it seems difficult for Tung Wah to defeat French Club. But if they can strengthen their defense and the forwards plan to connect on both wings, it will not be difficult to achieve victory. Tung Wah is eager to win the championship and will definitely plan well.

Although this match is not enough to determine who will win the championship, it is extremely important to the championship's success or failure. The future situation of this season's league can be summarized from this.

In addition, Kwong Nan vs. Portuguese on Sunday at Hongkou Park. Portuguese once won against West Postal by five to four, and West Postal lost to Kwong Nan by two to four. Based on this, it is not difficult for Kwong Nan to win three consecutive matches. The team's soccer skills have improved significantly recently, and their connections are quite impressive. The Portuguese team's strength is not as good as before due to the departure of Costa and Colasa.

Youth and Middle-aged Basketball Shooting Competition - Registration Closes Tonight - Competition Starts at 7 PM Tomorrow Night - Further Explanation of Competition and Scoring Methods

The public basketball shooting competition organized by the Youth and Middle-aged Association is scheduled to be held tomorrow night in the gymnasium of its Sichuan Road Clubhouse. However, as this competition is not yet popular in Shanghai, the number of participants has not been very enthusiastic. To encourage participation, the Association has specially prepared exquisite trophies displayed in the clubhouse's public exhibition area. To promote the event, the registration period has been extended, and registration is still possible until 9 PM tonight. Regardless of the number of participants, the competition will proceed as scheduled. Basketball shooting is the first step in practicing basketball. Shanghai is not short of basketball masters, and it is hoped that they will participate to spark interest in honing their skills. The competition rules and scoring methods are explained in detail below:

(1) One-Minute Close-Range Shot: Players stand at any point under the basket, ready to shoot. Upon hearing the referee's command, they begin shooting. The time limit is one minute. Each successful shot scores one point.

(2) Standing Long-Range Shot: Men stand 25 feet from the basket, and women and teenagers stand 20 feet from the basket. There are five designated spots. Each shot is taken once, and each successful shot scores five points.

(3) One-and-a-Half-Minute Dribbling: There are five designated spots under the basket. Players stand at the first spot, ready to dribble. Upon the referee's command, they begin dribbling and shooting. After shooting from each spot, regardless of whether the shot is successful, the player must dribble the ball back to the second spot, and then dribble and shoot from the second to the third, fourth, and fifth spots, following the designated order. The time limit is one and a half minutes. Each successful shot scores two points.

(4) Ten Free Throws: Taken from the free-throw line. Each successful shot scores three points.

(5) Long-Range Shot and Follow-Up: The spots are the same as for the standing long-range shot. Players start from the first spot and proceed in order. Each spot has one long-range shot and one follow-up shot. At the start, after the long-range shot, regardless of whether it is successful, the player immediately follows up to retrieve the ball and shoot again. However, after receiving the ball, the player may not dribble forward or walk with the ball. Any violation will invalidate the shot, even if successful. Each successful shot scores three points for the long-range shot and two points for the follow-up shot.

The champion is the player with the highest total score from the five categories. A runner-up and third-place winner will also be decided. If there is a tie in scores, the tie will be broken by another one-minute close-range shot.

Educational News

Cultural Circles Tensely Supporting Suiyuan

The Shanghai cultural circles' support association for the suppression of bandits in Suiyuan, since its establishment, convened a standing committee meeting a few days ago and decided to carry out various fundraising methods. It is now learned that, to actively promote this, the association has first designated persons in charge of each unit to separately make contact, and is rushing to produce receipts for submission to designated banks to collect donations. Once the preparatory procedures are completed, the association will convene persons in charge of each unit to discuss practical implementation methods. Various schools, bookstores, and cultural organizations have already begun to raise funds to meet the urgent needs of the front lines.

Fudan University: The entire faculty and students of Fudan University are sparing no effort in supporting Suiyuan. President Qian Xinzhi and Vice President Wu Nanxuan initiated a "Thrifty National Salvation Movement," with three methods: thrifty boxes, thrifty coupons, and thrifty banquets. It is said that the thrifty coupons are being actively printed and will be available for sale soon. The thrifty box was inaugurated yesterday morning after the flag-raising ceremony on the large playground. The Vice President first described the general idea of the significance of thrifty national salvation, stating that supporting Suiyuan and saving the nation lies in active persistence, and that there is no better method than thrifty national salvation. He then described the use of the thrifty box: all donations to the box should be placed in small envelopes, and donors should write their name, address, and donation amount on both sides of the envelope. The box will be opened publicly once a week. Wu then threw the savings from President Qian, Professor Ren Lifu, and himself, as well as the savings from the school's banquet for faculty and staff, into the box. Subsequently, Dean of Academic Affairs Zhang Yi, Professor Sun Hanbing, and students and workers flocked to the thrifty box and threw in their respective savings.

Tongji University: Students at Tongji University launched a fundraising campaign to support Suiyuan. The first round of donations, with over 400 participants, was remitted on the 17th. In the second round, class leaders from each grade expanded the fundraising efforts, and faculty and staff donated one day's salary, raising over 700 yuan, which was also sent directly to Suiyuan through the Bank of China on the 20th, along with a telegram expressing encouragement to fight to the end. The affiliated vocational school and middle school are still raising funds for future remittances.

Jiaotong University: All faculty, staff, and workers of Jiaotong University in this city have decided to donate one day's salary to comfort the soldiers in Suiyuan, totaling over 1,700 yuan. The money has already been sent to Beijing for transfer. The students have also made separate arrangements. Furthermore, the faculty and students of the School of Management of the university donated 150 yuan, saved from dining expenses.

Overseas Chinese Students of Jinan University: The Sumatra Students Association of National Jinan University held a general meeting yesterday, resolving to send a telegram to comfort the soldiers fighting against the enemy in Suiyuan. Furthermore, the association expressed extreme indignation at the Dutch East Indies government's arrest of Chinese community leaders on the 4th of this month, and specially requested the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to find ways to rescue the arrested overseas Chinese.

Tao Chung Girls' Middle School: Teachers at Tao Chung Girls' Middle School on Avenue Road are contributing a percentage of their salaries, as originally stipulated, and middle and primary school students have also set a minimum amount to contribute, to comfort the soldiers on the front lines fighting for the country. Yesterday was also the school's English speech competition final. The judges were Zhao Qiyu, Guo Xiufeng, Li Ruihua, and Weng Guoxun. The results were: first place, Ding Yuhui; second place, Zhou Baozhu; third place, Wang Shuzhen.

(Tianjin, 23rd) A student movement to drive out President Lu Fu and Dean of Academic Affairs Mo Yizhen has erupted at the Tianjin French Business College. Zhenjiang Middle School Student Killed While Building Road in Jiangsu Province - Zhang Chengde Dies

On the morning of the 22nd, teachers and military instructors of Zhenjiang Middle School in Jiangsu Province led first-year junior high school students to the new school site in Huangshan to build a road. At around 9 AM, while they were using a roller to flatten the road base, they tried to avoid a truck transporting goods. The road was uneven, and they could not signal in time. The teacher Zheng Qian, the military instructor Song Shuzhen, and the student Zhang Chengde, who were pulling the roller, all fell down the slope. The roller also rolled uncontrollably downwards. The student Zhang Chengde was unfortunately hit by the roller and severely injured. The teacher and military instructor escaped unharmed. The student suffered severe brain trauma and could not be saved. He died that evening at the Christian Hospital.

Jiangsu Education Department Seeks Movie Scripts - "Sunset Over a Lonely City" by Wang Pingling and Wang Mengou Selected

The Jiangsu Education Department's solicitation of educational film scripts has yielded remarkable results. The second selected script, "The Heart of a Loving Mother" by Wang Pingling, has already been handed over to the Shanghai Star Film Company for filming. The result of the current solicitation is that "Sunset Over a Lonely City," a collaboration between Wang Pingling and Wang Mengou, has been selected. The drama is based on the story of Tang general Zhang Xun's isolated army defending Suiyang, resisting An Lushan of the Jie tribe, and the people's oath to die rather than surrender. It also tells the story of Nan Jiyun breaking through the siege to seek help, and ultimately dying for the country when supplies ran out and reinforcements failed to arrive. The entire play is tragic, heroic, and intensely gripping, making it a famous historical drama relevant to modern times. It is said that, for the sake of prudence, the department intends to entrust the production to the Hejia Company, but this is still under consideration.

Shanghai Art College - 25th Anniversary Ceremony

The Shanghai Art College held its 25th anniversary ceremony yesterday morning at 10 AM. The ceremony was very grand, attended by heads of party and government agencies, guests, school board members, Minister of Education Wang, Mayor Wu, Director Pan, Ye Gongchuo, Xiao Youmei, Zhang Shouyong, Zhang Yuanruo, Shen Xinqing, and over a thousand students, parents, alumni, faculty, and staff. The ceremony began with solemnity and order amid the melodious sounds of strings.

Principal's Report

After the meeting began, Principal Liu Haisu first reported that the school was founded in the first year of the Republic of China, born at the same time as the Republic of China. From the first year of the Republic of China to the present, it has been a period of great transformation for our country's political system. The Art College was born at this time, shouldering the mission of emerging art. In the history of art, it also marks a great divide. Over the past 25 years, we have worked hard to build it up. Fortunately, with the support of society, we have achieved today's scale. In the future, we will continue to uphold the inherent culture of the past, absorb new Western art ideas, observe the trends of the times, and understand the future of life, so that we can create art that represents the soul of the times, and inspire the great personality and independent spirit of our people. This is the great mission that all members of this school are committed to working hard to achieve. We hope that society will continue to support and guide us to complete it.

Ye Gongchuo's Speech

Our school has been established for 25 years. Our country's art schools began with this. Our school has always embraced the promotion of national culture and has always adhered to this proposition. Today, the country is declining. This determination is not only a responsibility that a single school or a single person should bear, nor can it be fully exerted by a single school or a single person. However, looking around at art schools in the East, West, South, and North, there is more than just this one school. However, judging from the proof of facts, our school is in a leading position, and it has also devoted the most effort to the country and the nation in the past. I have always advocated national salvation based on one's own position. The so-called position is the meaning of self-reliance. We are standing from the standpoint of art, and we should work hard in the field of art to assist the country and the nation in moving forward. Minister of Education Wang then spoke on behalf of Xiao Youmei, and Mayor Wu spoke on behalf of Zhang Yuanruo. Both encouraged the school to promote the movement of cultural renaissance in our country in order to realize the renaissance of the nation. Representatives from the municipal party headquarters and the municipal social affairs bureau, as well as school board member Zhang Shouyong, successively gave speeches, commending and encouraging the school. Finally, representatives of faculty, alumni, and students delivered congratulatory speeches, and the meeting adjourned with music. The venue was filled with congratulatory gifts from all walks of life. The Boy Scouts of Danhua Elementary School and the military training students of the school assisted in maintaining order at the venue.

Exhibition Situation

The memorial exhibition held by the school was on its third day yesterday. The nineteen rooms were divided into five major sections: (1) Painting Reference Section, with over a hundred exquisitely printed works by famous artists from various schools since the European Renaissance to the present, all the same size as the originals. This is a unique opportunity to study and appreciate art history. (2) Recent Works by Domestic Famous Artists; (3) Recent Works by Professors; (4) Achievements of Previous Graduates; (5) Achievements of Current Students. The celebration banquet was reportedly held last night at the Yihai Tang, attended by hundreds of school board members, faculty, staff, alumni, students, and their families. The lights were brilliant, and there was lively conversation, with entertainment adding to the atmosphere. A student-initiated entertainment show will be held at the Lake Society on Beijing Road at 7 PM tonight, with very exciting performances.

Literacy School Headmaster Meeting

Investigating Out-of-School People – Assisted by the Public Security Bureau - Domestic Servants, Shop Employees – Group Enrollment This city’s Literacy Education Committee convened a meeting of the headmasters of various central literacy schools the other day. Attending were Executive Director Jiang Jianbai, Chief of General Affairs Section Song Yaochen, Chief of Management Section Cheng Fengxiang, Chief of Supervision Section Lu Guangao, Chief of Labor Education Section Wang Gang, Inspectors Wu Zhengqin, Zhang Shuqin, Liu Zhongyi, Liu Qimin, and the headmasters of various schools Chuan Depei, Huang Yaohua, Feng Xiancheng, Xu Bingkun, Feng Baogen, Zhou Yuanlong, and others, totaling over ten people. Executive Director Jiang chaired the meeting, and Liu Qimin recorded the minutes. There were many important matters discussed: (1) The investigation of out-of-school people should be conducted in stages and assisted by the Public Security Bureau. (2) Employers should facilitate the enrollment of domestic servants and shop employees, and those who arbitrarily make things difficult or prevent enrollment will be punished according to regulations. (3) Out-of-school people who delay enrollment or are absent from class after being notified will be severely punished according to regulations. (4) Factories, companies, and shops with 30 or more out-of-school people must establish labor literacy schools. (5) Inspections will still be divided into general and class inspections, conducted separately by the Supervision Section and the headmasters of various schools. The headmasters may also exchange areas for mutual observation. It is also reported that the Management Section of the association is currently revising the past regulations, which were too broad, and will submit them to the municipal government for approval and promulgation after completion. Furthermore, the Supervision Section has recently developed many new practical regulations and forms for verification, and future supervision will be greatly improved, with significant results.

Commercial News

Yarn - Spot Sales Show Signs of Improvement - Cotton Yarn Price Increase Still Fierce

The yarn market continues to rise, and the momentum is still tense. The reason is that yarn sales have improved, and buyers from Tianjin, the interior, Changsha, Guangdong, and other regions are very enthusiastic. Spot yarn is extremely tight, so many parties are actively involved. However, the gold industry has released a large amount, and some have already gone short. However, those who absorb it are still pouring in. However, with the clouds of war looming in Suiyuan, the transaction volume has greatly increased, and the future changes are difficult to predict. Dachangcheng and Changfeng are selling 10,000 to 15,950 bales.

Speculative Yarn Shorts Also Eager to Cover

The speculative yarn market opened lower due to the serious war situation in Suiyuan. It was hoped that the labor unrest would be resolved, and the gold industry continued to sell off. The current month fell by four corners, a continuous drop of one yuan and four and six corners. In the second round, there was a slight rebound. By the third close, it was reported that Tianjin, Changsha, and Guangdong buyers, seeing the improvement in spot yarn sales and the firmness of raw cotton, suddenly increased their buying, and the market quickly turned upwards with good momentum, trending higher again. As a result, the closing prices for each month were up one yuan to one yuan and four and six corners compared to the previous day's closing price. The market remained tense after the afternoon opening. Because the labor unrest in the Japanese factories has not been completely resolved, and spot yarn transactions are smooth, shorts are eager to cover, and the rise is particularly strong. At the close, it was reported that yarn sales were over 2,700 bales. As a result, the closing prices for each month rose another nine corners to one yuan and seven corners compared to the morning closing price. Yuda sold in the morning and bought in the afternoon. It was found that Changfeng had settled 15,950 bales of long positions, Dachangcheng 10,000 bales, Dafu 1,700 bales, Changji 1,950 bales, Fengtai 1,100 bales, Fukang 1,850 bales, Taichang 2,000 bales, Dachang 1,400 bales, and Jinchang 800 bales. Mingde bought 4,900 bales, Yiji 2,000 bales, Dafeng 1,000 bales, Heyu 2,650 bales, Guangfeng 5,700 bales, Shenji 6,150 bales, Renfeng 1,250 bales, Wang Taixing 1,900 bales, Xincheng 3,800 bales, and Tonghe 1,600 bales. The highest and lowest prices and the closing prices for the day are listed on the left.

Yarn Sales of Over 2,700 Bales

Spot yarn sales are brisk. It was found that buyers purchased a total of 2,785 bales from various firms throughout the day, with prices rising by two yuan. The buying volume of each firm is as follows:

Tianjin 720, Jiangxi 30, Inland 675, Nanjing 10

Sichuan 250, Changsha 365, Shantou 10

Guangdong 480, Yunnan 30, Peers 25

Cotton - Long Positions and Short Covering Rise Together - Forward Prices Have Exceeded the Two Yuan Mark

The cotton market saw both US cotton and Indian cotton rebound, and the yarn market was brisk, which boosted confidence. Flour companies and securities companies continued to increase their positions, leading to a shortage of supply. At the same time, factory demand showed some signs of improvement, and market prices moved forward step by step. The forward month price has broken through the two yuan mark.

Speculative Flowers - Consistent Dragging by Non-Industry Players

The speculative flower market opened with a tight and lively atmosphere, as several yarn factories had already resumed production, and short positions were covering in the near term. There was a lack of sellers in the market, and the market was firm. In addition, US cotton forward prices rebounded by 20 points and Indian cotton also rose by 1.2 rupees, making the market even stronger. Market prices advanced step by step, with forward months breaking through the two yuan mark. As a result, the closing prices for each month rose by 0.3 to 0.55 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. Due to the consistent dragging by outside investors and large players, the market became even stronger and buying interest was very strong after the afternoon opening. However, some, due to the good harvest of this Geng year, were still selling off when prices rose. As a result, the closing prices for each month rose another 0.15 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was found that Dafu sold 6,300 dan, Jinchang 6,800 dan, Taixing 3,5900 dan, Xingchang 6,900 dan, Shenji 2,700 dan, Changfeng 6,000 dan, Dachang 10,900 dan, Shengyuan 7,900 dan, Xinchang 7,100 dan, Yuanxingchang 7,400 dan, Changhe 2,500 dan, Fengtai 2,000 dan, and Hengchang 4,300 dan. Jinghua bought 3,000 dan, Tonghe 2,000 dan, Yuda 4,900 dan, Tongji 2,800 dan, Mingde 8,600 dan, Zhenda 5,100 dan, Gengfeng 10,800 dan, Renfeng 7,200 dan, Dachangcheng 5,800 dan, Runkang 14,000 dan, Xiecheng 2,500 dan, Fukang 4,900 dan, Hexing 2,700 dan, and Senkang 2,700 dan. The highest and lowest prices and the closing prices for the day are listed on the left.

Factory demand is active, with a source of 1,180 bales of Yao flower and 958 bales of Tong flower.

Silk and Tea Silk Transactions Were Quite Quiet Yesterday

Yesterday, Yokohama was closed for a holiday, and New York was also observing Sunday, so the Shanghai market became quiet. There were few white silk piece goods sold for export, with limited transactions. Gray fabrics were selling somewhat, and other printing houses also made sporadic purchases. Market prices did not fluctuate significantly. Raw silk transactions were still difficult to facilitate. Silk prices were stable, with a total of 149 bales sold citywide.

Sugar Market: The Price of Medium Granulated White Sugar Increases Again

Yesterday, the grain market trend was flat. The guild's price for spot No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar was 21.6 yuan, ordinary re-export goods were 6.1 yuan, re-export Dutch red KD mark were 5.5 yuan, and AW mark were 5.3 yuan, all with transactions. There was not much change in Dongbai (Eastern White Sugar), except for No. 8 YT mark re-export, which traded at 6.1 yuan, a slight increase of 5 cents. Mianbai No. 1 from the Zhenji factory was 20.4 yuan. Chaoqing (Chaozhou Green Sugar) was quoted in a Shantou dispatch as requiring 13.5 yuan, an increase of 3 cents compared to the previous price. Yesterday was the first tender exchange period for Cantonese sugar this week for the Contract Company, with a total quota of over 8,000 bags. The tender price for medium granulated white sugar rose again to 19.3 yuan, with no other changes. 1,140 bags of coarse white sugar from the Shunde Five Rams factory were sold at 21.3 yuan, and another 110 bags from the City New Factory at 21.1 yuan, and 155 bags from Shantou at 20.9 yuan.

Spring Cloth Sales Already Underway; Prices Mostly Higher Than Last Year; Yesterday's Market Saw All Goods Rise With Yarn Prices

Yesterday, although the labor unrest in the cotton cloth market has largely subsided, the demand for yarn is strong and prices are rising. Speculative yarn for all months is also rising uniformly. The current stock of cotton cloth is depleted, and the market is still calling for goods. Due to the high cost of raw materials and yarn, few goods are being held back. Yesterday, cotton merchants were firm, and out-of-town buyers were still actively purchasing, especially for goods destined for southern routes, Sichuan, Yunnan, Changsha, Hankou, Jiujiang, Dagukou, and Wuhu, which are considered good destinations. Sales in Ningbo, Shaoxing, and this street are also brisk. Transactions are mostly for white goods, lightweight coarse cloth, fine cloth, and fine twill. Money crepe and flannel are also selling surprisingly well. Although the sales of printed flannel are still good, prices remain sluggish, with hand-made goods being sold at a discount of five to one fen per yard compared to factory prices. Recently, spring goods such as pongee and bleached cloth have been attracting inquiries from flat street vendors and dyeing factories. However, due to the high price of yarn, weaving factories would need to increase the price of pongee by five to six fen per yard and bleached/striped cloth by more than one yuan per piece compared to last year's prices, causing many to remain hesitant. This year, due to very good sales, factories have very little pongee left. A few factories have already opened their prices, which are said to be five fen per yard higher than before.

Woolen Goods Prices Rising Endlessly

Yesterday, the trade in woolen goods was strong, and the trend was bullish. Both out-of-town buyers and local merchants were purchasing. Trading houses have dispatched considerable amounts of seasonal winter goods. Shipments from Pudong and Puxi have been quite congested in recent days. However, those holding the goods are extremely cautious about extending credit, especially to out-of-town buyers. The prices of woolen goods in the guild have been rising endlessly in about 70% to 80% of cases. Those holding the goods are generally optimistic, and the gradual increase in prices is rare in recent years.

Yesterday, with pure gold holding steady, the gold market saw strong buying interest, including from outside the industry, which briefly boosted the market. Major sellers profited from the high prices, resulting in a decline. In the morning, overseas silver markets saw London rising and the US remaining unchanged. Forward silver prices in Montevideo rose by five and a half to seven li. Exchange rates rose slightly. London spot gold was unchanged. The Central Bank's posted rates showed both English and American rates unchanged. The Customs Gold Unit was unchanged. The posted price for standard speculative gold remained 1156.1 yuan. The market opened high, and buyers continued to exert pressure, with suppliers remaining cautious, briefly boosting the market. Later, major players took advantage of the high prices to sell, causing a gradual decline. HSBC's posted rates showed both English and American rates unchanged and then gradually falling. The silver balancing tax rose by 1.125 fen. Although there was a rebound, buyers gradually thinned out, and major short sellers were active. The market weakened by midday. Later trading was sparse, with the market initially steady but then weakening, largely due to major players becoming more willing to sell. Yesterday's swaps saw the bulls posting 1.65 yuan. Securities: Only One Market Day Remaining in This Month; Public Bond Swap Transactions Very Frequent; Market Price Changed From Weak To Firm…Mixed Rise and Fall

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, the public bond market, because it was the last two days of futures trading for this month, swap transactions were extremely mixed. The trend changed from weak to firm and bullish. Initially, due to unfavorable news about the situation, the market felt increasingly weak and sluggish. The selling sentiment on the floor was strong, and market prices gradually declined. However, later, short sellers eagerly swapped positions, and many retail investors also covered their short positions, causing the market to rebound. Today is the last day of November futures trading. In this unsettling environment, both bulls and bears are still engaging in significant competition. However, based on the trend on the floor, there is a risk of a short squeeze. Yesterday morning, the market opened with the news of the intense fighting in the Sui region causing panic. Major players such as 47 and 14 were selling heavily, and retail investors followed suit. The supply on the floor was overwhelming, and market prices uniformly declined by 2 to 4.5 jiao. In the second session, the market slightly rebounded. Swap transactions were very active, and major players such as 4 and 10 swapped even more. Grains: Wheat Supply Not Smooth; Flour Market Feels Particularly Firm

Yesterday in the flour market, after the morning opening, all months showed a uniform upward trend. The quotation for foreign wheat saw Chicago near-term up 2 jiao, far-term down 0.4 jiao, and Canada down about 1 jiao. At the opening, sentiment for this month was initially calm, but starting with February, sentiment gradually became active because the combined price of current foreign wheat never broke, and the arrival of domestic wheat was impeded due to blockades everywhere. As a result, both internal and external thinking turned bullish. Buying interest also gradually became brisk, increasing by 1 to 2 fen compared to the previous week's closing price. Until the afternoon opening, this month initially saw a short-covering rally, reaching a high of 3.83 yuan. Trading for December and beyond was very brisk. Due to minor selling by major players, the market stabilized. After the second session, sentiment calmed down, falling slightly below the initial opening. After that, the trend was to fluctuate, with not much movement. Those in the industry speculated that with the arrival of wheat gradually decreasing, there would be a shortage of raw materials, so the subsequent trend should be long-term stability.

Yesterday in the speculative wheat market, after the morning opening, all months were uniformly stable and firm. Oil Market: Rare in Twenty Years, Tallow Oil Dealers Actively

Tallow oil foreign trade, from the present, twenty years ago, during the early Republic of China period, around 1915-1916, during the European War, in the era of the old Russian Empire, they procured huge quantities from our country. Since then, only Dongyang Zhuang has slightly exported some each year, but the quantities are extremely small, having almost no impact on the market. But this time, just at the time of metabolism, European and American foreign firms are widely purchasing in Hankou and Yichang, etc., for delivery in December and January, with a total of 700-800 tons of transactions. This massive export business has not occurred in twenty years. This sudden event has surprised all those engaged in this business, and the market has suddenly jumped by 2-3 yuan. Moreover, new goods have not flourished in the Hankou market, and old oil has been exhausted, creating a stormy scenario in the market. The prices at which manufacturers are selling to foreign firms are kept secret and cannot be investigated. According to various foreign firms in this port, they have also begun purchasing, but not in the huge quantities of the Hankou market. The production areas are at the peak of output. If only for domestic sales, there would certainly be a surplus. If they also want to supply foreign firms, there may be a shortage. Therefore, whether the market can rise again depends on the continued purchasing of foreign firms and ourselves. Currently, all the oil firms in this city have no inventory. Demand is about to move, and goods are not arriving, resulting in a severe shortage of oil. It is estimated that the selling price of Wumu Chongjing must be above 24 yuan per dan, and Macheng oil must also be around 22 yuan per dan.

A Call for the Health of Children in Rural and Township Elementary Schools Nationwide (Part 2)

— Xie Yuheng

4. The School Hygiene Needs of Rural and Township Elementary Schools in China Today

School hygiene is the guarantee of children's health and the tool to promote physical soundness. Whether it is urban or rural elementary schools, it is equally needed. Urban schools and students have more facilities to help guarantee health due to the environment of material civilization. All aspects are much more convenient than rural schools and students. According to the statistics of the Health Department, more than 90% of students in urban elementary schools are unhealthy. There are no hospitals and health agencies as perfect as those in urban areas in rural towns, and there are not that many medical personnel. It can be simply said that there are none in rural areas. School teachers only know how to teach. No one cares about children's health problems. The call for universal school hygiene facilities to seek happiness for children only stays in a few cities. Children's Year has passed, and the Children's Welfare Committee has been abolished. Children in rural areas and urban children spend Children's Year in the same way, but they experience two different scenarios. Urban children have been given many happy careers by Children's Year. Children in rural areas still live the same impoverished and sick life. They are not disappointed. They are still desiring the mercy of powerful administrative officials to seek some happiness for them with political power, especially the urgent health problems.

School hygiene in urban areas is easier to implement because of the assistance of environmental aspects. At the same time, the experts, doctors, and nurses are influenced by material civilization and bathed in Western culture. They admire the prosperity of cities, and at the same time, cities can give them the needs of their own desires anytime and anywhere, so they all live in cities. Therefore, school hygiene facilities in urban areas are much easier than in rural towns. In terms of talent, specialized talents are nostalgic for the city, which does not affect the school hygiene facilities in rural towns. The school hygiene facilities in rural towns in China today do not need those talents who admire urban life and admire Westernization. They can not only adapt to rural work but also easily infect the students in rural towns, making the students uneasy in the countryside and incompetent in the city, which in turn affects education. A certain city elementary school once asked the author to hire a school health nurse for them. The author believed that this type of talent must have received specialized training to be able to take office, so they wanted to introduce a nurse who had received public health training and discussed it with the school. The school rejected it because they had hired a person with the same qualifications before and found that they did not meet the needs. The reason was that the health work they did in the school failed to participate in the national conditions and implemented it. They completely implemented a set of Western-style health formulas there. Public opinion arose in the society, and they could not get through everywhere. Moreover, they did not consider the school's economy and the improvement of the environment, and did not start with trying to improve it with a small amount of economy to make it in line with hygiene principles, but instead took the principle of demolishing and rebuilding. No wonder the school rejected my introduction of this type of qualified talent when they saw it? This type of health talent cannot even be accommodated in the city. How can they serve the countryside? Once the hygiene of rural and township elementary schools is actively promoted and implemented, public health nurses will inevitably be needed to assist in the work. It is asked how many training institutions in the country can provide this type of talent suitable for rural work. No wonder people say, "Rural hygiene is very important, but it is difficult to train talents. A rural health worker is much stronger than an urban one, and their position is much higher."

Implementing hygiene in rural and township elementary schools is not only a difficult task to hire talents, but also the economy of school hygiene is a very big problem. Specialized talents cannot be hired. At the very least, there must be a public health nurse who can serve as the instructor for several schools' hygiene. Each province should open large-scale rural and township elementary schools, school hygiene training classes, and train the current rural and township elementary school teachers. Anyone who has done school hygiene feels that school hygiene must be handled automatically by teachers. Not only can it save money, but it can also increase work efficiency. How can we train teachers to meet the needs of hygiene in rural and township elementary schools? It all depends on the experience and talent of the trainers. The hygiene expenses of elementary schools in rural and township areas should try to avoid collecting from students as much as possible. The hygiene fee of five or six yuan per semester is enough. The school hygiene facilities focus entirely on health education and health care work. The improvement of the school environment can use the activities of teachers and students. In short, when training, pay attention to "being suitable for the rural environment." Do not teach the rural teachers European and American or Japanese-style hygiene that does not conform to Chinese rural towns, otherwise, not only is there no way to deal with the economy, but it is also a waste of training. If the school cannot even afford a medicine cabinet, the education administration should find a way to subsidize it.

5. Promoting Political Power

The implementation of school hygiene facilities in rural and township elementary schools is directly and indirectly very important for China's revival. How can we find a way to achieve it in the shortest possible time? It all depends on the promotion of political power. As long as the government takes this matter seriously, establishes the direction of implementation, and strictly implements it with political power, children in rural and township elementary schools across the country can soon get health guarantees.

It is found that the Ministry of Education has already promulgated the school hygiene facility program. Due to the lack of talent, most places have not followed it. From this point of view, we are requesting the education authorities for the children of rural and township elementary schools across the country to first add rural and township elementary school hygiene training classes in each province and train a large number of incumbent teachers in rural and township elementary schools. The Ministry of Education should set up commissioners to manage this matter. The education departments of each province should have this director of the establishment, and also the responsibility of supervision. The county education bureaus should also have the director of the establishment. The observation and inspection of school hygiene should be as important as school administration and teaching. In this way, the implementation of school hygiene facilities will be supervised, and it will not be allowed to be neglected or spread out for a long time without being realized.

6. Conclusion

From today's rural hygiene work, there are too few who truly seek health guarantees for children in rural and township elementary schools. China is now in such a serious time, and revival work is so important. We must not only care about the health problems of urban children and ignore the health problems of the majority of children in rural and township elementary schools. Ignoring the health of children in rural and township elementary schools is also equivalent to ignoring the work of reviving China.

The number of people calling for the health of children in rural and township elementary schools is increasing, which is enough to show the importance of this issue. If we rely on rural hygiene to promote it, this snail-like walk is not suitable for survival in today's era. The current hygiene in rural and township elementary schools needs to be realized universally in the shortest possible time.

Training rural and township elementary school teachers to serve in school hygiene work is not only in line with the national conditions, but also can increase work efficiency.

Administrative officials! Experts! Gentlemen of the Children's Affairs Committee! Please find a solution to the health problems of children in rural and township elementary schools.

The Problem of Building the Nursing Profession in China Tomorrow (Part 1)

— Li Lingdong

As we promote the development of medical and health endeavors in China, it would be a grave error to focus solely on the expansion of medicine and pharmaceuticals while neglecting the integrated promotion of nursing and midwifery. In recent years, disputes often arise between the public and the new medical community, leading to litigation. This is partly due to the public's lack of understanding of medical and pharmaceutical principles and insufficient knowledge of medical and health hygiene. However, conflicts also arise significantly due to poor nursing skills and a lack of humility in nursing attitudes. Therefore, advocating for the nursing profession and reforming nursing education are as important and closely related as reforming medical education. I will now briefly discuss the issue of building the nursing profession in China tomorrow.

First, the independence of nursing schools is a fundamental principle.

Nursing schools are the place for educating nursing talent. Only with excellent and well-equipped facilities can talent be trained and ideal nurses be produced. Undoubtedly, nursing schools must first be independent. With the independence of nursing schools, all administrative authority over nursing and the promotion of the nursing profession can be established on a solid foundation. With a foundation as solid as iron and stone, the nursing profession can gradually engage in social advocacy, making society aware of the significance and importance of the nursing profession. Then, the future of the nursing profession will have hope for progress.

Many nursing schools in China appear to be independent on the surface, but in reality, they are not. All authority within the schools remains under the control of hospitals. At this stage, we cannot resolutely overturn the existing situation because it is a sign of the transitional period for nursing schools and a process of their evolution. However, we cannot allow them to remain perpetually in this transitional era. At least, there must be a final limit, and we must seek the era of independence for our nursing schools, reaching the ideal generation we envision.

That generation of ideal nurses, the engine of this great mission, is entirely dependent on the Nursing Education Committee, which bears the highest administrative authority over nursing in China. Efforts must be made to persuade the highest educational administrative authority in China—the Ministry of Education—to recognize the nursing profession as an important form of vocational education. It should issue orders to each province and city to establish at least one nursing school, on par with specialized vocational schools, to cultivate nursing talent and promote the development of the nursing profession. If this construction is successful, all provinces and cities in China will have established nursing schools, and even remote areas can enjoy the services of the nursing profession, benefiting patients. When the nursing profession achieves widespread socialization, then the future of the nursing profession will have a strong grip and a bright future.

Second, the construction of the nursing education system is the catalyst for reform.

Every profession is a product of society. Why are some professions considered noble and respected, while others are seen as lowly and inferior? This can be attributed to the distinctions created by thought and knowledge, which lead to class differences. For example, civil engineers and carpenters both engage in similar work with a common goal, yet civil engineers enjoy a significantly higher social status. Carpenters, who also work on civil engineering projects, are often regarded as having a lower social standing. The clear answer is that civil engineers have received rigorous knowledge transfer and extensive training, while carpenters blindly follow procedures without understanding the underlying principles. Therefore, the status of a profession is entirely determined by intellectual capacity and the level of education, dictating the fate of the profession. We cannot deny this and must instead encourage the newly emerging nursing profession to be vigilant.

We know that the training of any profession encompasses several stages. For example, graduates of senior high school normal schools can further their studies at university normal schools or colleges of education, pursuing advanced research in education.

However, when we look at the nursing education system, graduates of advanced nursing vocational schools have no opportunities for further study. This is the final destination for nurses seeking knowledge, a dead end where they spend their lives.

At the same time, nursing instructors in nursing schools have not received adequate teacher training and lack practical teaching skills. The knowledge imparted to nursing students and their nursing skills are vague and unable to meet the actual needs of clinical nursing and alleviate the suffering of patients. So, where will we produce specialized nursing teachers and train talent to inspect nurses?
