Common Sense on Hygiene for Eye, Ear, Nose, and Throat Diseases

— Tang Renjin

(108) Cornea

The cornea is commonly known as the "black of the eye." It is a transparent membrane that forms the front part of the eyeball. It is shaped like a horizontal ellipse, curved forward to form part of the eye's surface. Its diameter is 10 millimeters, its transverse diameter is 11 millimeters, and its thickness is 1 millimeter. The structure of the cornea can be divided into five layers: the epithelial cell layer (composed of brick-like epithelial cells), the anterior basement membrane (or Bowman's membrane, a thin, structureless transparent membrane), the corneal stroma (the substance layer, composed of very fine connective tissue fibers), the posterior basement membrane (or Descemet's membrane, a structureless elastic membrane), and the endothelium (composed of larger, flat cells). The surface of the cornea is constantly moistened by tears, so it remains smooth, facilitating the entry and refraction of light. In its normal physiological state, the cornea's surface is smooth. However, if a pathological change occurs, it becomes rough. The degree of roughness varies, sometimes subtle and sometimes significant, depending on the condition. If the cornea suffers from inflammation or degenerative changes, it will become cloudy. Whether the cloudiness is fresh or old, located in the central or marginal region, deep or superficial, whether there is tissue loss, and whether it appears grayish-white or yellowish, are all closely related to the diagnosis and treatment of the disease. Most notably, fresh cloudiness is usually accompanied by irritation symptoms. Patients experience photophobia, tearing, and pain. At the same time, corneal congestion, conjunctival edema, and hypopyon may occur.

(109) Keratitis

There are many types of keratitis, and its condition is quite complex. Corneal congestion is its only major symptom, occurring in the early stages of inflammation. When the inflammation is severe, the sclera, iris, and conjunctiva are also often congested. Other major symptoms of keratitis include corneal cloudiness, neovascularization, corneal ulcer, and hypopyon. I will now briefly describe them separately as follows:

(1) Corneal Cloudiness - Corneal cloudiness is a necessary symptom of keratitis, caused by cell infiltration. The degree of cloudiness varies depending on the type of inflammation and the severity of the condition. It may appear like a mist, dots, or patches. Clinically, cloudiness can be divided into three types: thin and translucent cloudiness is called corneal nebula, slightly thicker and grayish-white cloudiness is called corneal macula, and thick and white cloudiness is called corneal leukoma.

(2) Neovascularization - In superficial keratitis, neovascularization often originates from the conjunctiva and is distributed on the surface of the cornea, often in a dendritic pattern. In deep keratitis, neovascularization often originates from the sclera and uvea and is distributed in the deeper layers, often in a brush-like or broom-like pattern.

(3) Corneal Ulcer - When corneal inflammation is severe, the tissue often breaks down, and the surface develops tissue loss, which is called a corneal ulcer.

(4) Hypopyon - In suppurative keratitis with ulceration, there is often hypopyon in the anterior chamber. The pus appears yellowish-white and settles at the bottom of the anterior chamber in a crescent shape, forming a horizontal plane above.

The patient's subjective symptoms include photophobia, tearing, foreign body sensation, burning sensation, pain, and visual impairment.

(110) Why does the amount of nasal secretions increase?

Nasal secretions are commonly known as nasal mucus. In a healthy and disease-free nasal cavity, the amount of secretions is normal. They do not flow out of the nostrils or down into the nasopharynx. However, if the nasal cavity suffers from acute or chronic rhinitis, sinusitis, vasomotor rhinitis, or nasal foreign bodies, the amount of nasal secretions can suddenly increase, either flowing out of the nostrils or down into the nasopharynx. The nature and quantity of nasal secretions vary depending on the pathogen, the condition, and the stage of the disease. I will now describe them separately as follows:

(1) In the early stages of acute rhinitis (commonly known as the common cold), the nasal mucosa is dry, but soon a large amount of serous nasal fluid flows. After a certain period of time, it becomes viscous, and finally, it becomes purulent and the amount decreases significantly.

(2) The secretions of sinusitis vary in nature. They can be serous, mucous, or purulent. Secretions from the anterior sinuses (maxillary sinus, frontal sinus, and anterior ethmoid air cells) mostly flow into the middle nasal meatus. Secretions from the posterior sinuses (sphenoid sinus and posterior ethmoid air cells) mostly flow into the olfactory cleft or down into the nasopharynx.

(3) Vasomotor Rhinitis - This is a nervous disorder that occurs in episodes. Only during an episode does it secrete a large amount of serous nasal fluid. Medically, it is called watery rhinorrhea. If a foreign body is present in the nasal cavity, the foreign body will first stimulate the secretion of mucus, followed by purulent secretions. It often has a foul odor.

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

Convolvulaceae

1. Bindweed Calystegia japonica, Chois.

(Plant) Grows naturally in the fields. A perennial vine. Leaves are alternate, long-stalked, sagittate lanceolate with pointed ends and auriculate feet. In summer, it bears pale red funnel-shaped flowers. The capsule is spherical.

(Crude Drug) Bindweed Herb Herba Calysteiae, collected as whole plant and dried.

(Ingredients) Whole plant (air-dried) contains 30.7% water-soluble substances, 17.5% glucose (increases to 30% after heating in dilute acid), and 4.3% ash. It also contains substances such as Saponin.

(Pharmacology) The decoction of the whole herb has a clear inhibitory effect on blood sugar in rabbits, concerning alimentary and adrenal hyperglycaemia.

(Medicinal use) Old saying: Bindweed is a diuretic and is effective for treating fatigue and tonifying essence.

Folk: Bindweed is effective for treating diabetes.

2. Dodder Cuscuta japonica, Chois

(Plant) Grows naturally in the fields. An annual parasitic vine. The stem is yellowish-brown, fleshy and brittle, parasitizing on woody plants by means of suckers, lacking leaves. Lateral spicate inflorescences, in summer blooms tubular 5 shallowly lobed yellowish-white small flowers. The capsule is small and broadly rounded.

(Crude drug) Dodder Seed Semen Cuscutae is collected as seed. The product is reddish-brown or dark brown, a slightly heart-shaped particle, only about 2 mm in diameter, 100 particles weighing 0.75 g. The product has a mild odor and an oily taste.

(Ingredients) The seeds contain a resinous glycoside.

(Medicinal use) Old saying: Dodder is a tonic and strengthening medicine. Daily dose is 8 g, taken internally as a decoction.

Folk: It is said that squeezing the juice from the stem and applying it to the face can remove freckles.

After Participating in the Smallpox Vaccination Campaign in the Shantytowns of the Jiangsu Provincial Capital

— Yin Baishui

I remember in the early summer of this year, there was a great commotion about this year being a "cholera year," and it was loudly proclaimed that it was particularly prevalent in the Yangtze River basin, causing widespread panic. Various health agencies were also very busy, because cholera is indeed too fierce and brutal when it breaks out. In the Jiangsu provincial capital, the provincial health bureau used all its energy to publicize and jointly with various health agencies to carry out expanded preventive injections, and the result can be considered a victory. The hot summer has long passed, and no bad news of cholera outbreaks has been heard. This must be attributed to the efforts of prevention and the value of prevention. Although autumn is not as "dreadful as summer," the outbreak of malignant malaria this autumn has threatened everyone with fear and trepidation. Now autumn has left the world, and everyone can breathe a deep sigh of relief. The coming winter and spring are generally considered to be peaceful days, but don't forget! Smallpox is already secretly and rapidly breeding and flourishing, and will be drawing its lines and starting its attack on mankind. If we do not catch up and prevent it—by vaccinating—its brutal tricks will not only make you an ugly pockmarked face, but also endanger your life. Looking at the facts of the past, each outbreak of smallpox has harmed countless promising children! On the national level, it has lost enormous vitality, and on the family level, it has lost its only lifeline. The Jiangsu Provincial Health Bureau had already seen this point, and in order to prevent problems before they occur, in addition to the special free vaccination in major hospitals and clinics, it also invited all the students of the Zhenjiang Rural Nursing School on November 8, divided into ten teams, each led by a health police officer, to the designated shantytowns in twenty areas to do vaccination work, while doing publicity work. However, because the people's knowledge is ignorant, their thinking is stubborn, and their health education is lacking, there are many difficulties. I would like to borrow a corner of this publication to publish it, hoping that the health authorities will study together to find a solution, and at the same time write down the心得after this vaccination to give to everyone, so that it may be of assistance in the future.

The difficulties of the work

(1) Because the weather is cold, people are unwilling to be vaccinated.

(2) They believe that one vaccination of earth pox (old-fashioned vaccination) can prevent it for life, while vaccination of foreign pox (cowpox) cannot. This misconception exists, so those who have been vaccinated with the old-fashioned method are unwilling to be vaccinated a second time, and those who have not been vaccinated ask for old-fashioned Chinese medicine.

(3) They believe that vaccination can cure diseases. If you say that it can only prevent smallpox and cannot cure diseases, they are unwilling to be vaccinated. If you want to comply with their psychology, you should say that it can cure diseases, which would violate health education. (To be continued)

Shanghai Newspaper Supplement

Talking Points

Map Drawing Competition

— Bin

The YMCA held a map drawing competition yesterday. It is said that there are two ways to compete. One is to select one or several provinces in the country and draw a map of (1) those that occupy an important position in the national economy; (2) those that occupy an important relationship in national defense; (3) those with fertile land, suitable for immigration; (4) those with significant development potential in the future; (5) those with abundant products and many exports. The other is to select one or several provinces and draw a map of (1) rivers; (2) mountain ranges; (3) important place names; (4) important railways and waterways; (5) important products; (6) important commercial ports. As for the evaluation criteria, they will be based on accuracy, importance, neatness, completeness, and usefulness.

This is a very meaningful and interesting competition. Saying it is meaningful, I think this does not need me to explain, readers will nod their heads in agreement; saying it is interesting, then I think as long as people who really feel the joy of working will definitely be able to experience it. To give an example, you might as well take the exam in school as an example. In school, if you do particularly well in a certain subject, when you are taking the exam, and after the exam, your mental pleasure is really indescribable. It not only compensates for your hard work buried in your desk, but at that time, you even think of the situation when you were diligently buried in your desk, and that hard work will also turn into pleasure.

But the map drawing competition is not like a school exam. Even if you are the best "top student" in the school exam, it does not mean that you like every subject, but in order to "graduate" or "upgrade", you have to accept the "cramming" homework, so the result is that the exam is not only not liked by you, but sometimes it makes you feel afraid, so the exam that could have encouraged you to compete upwards is also avoided because of fear and disgust.

The greater benefit of the map drawing competition, of course, lies in its meaning, just as its origin says; "...If we broaden our horizons and say that the country is our big family, who would say it is not appropriate. We should know the property and things in the family like the back of our hand. If we cannot know the details, we will lose the basis for survival, and the people of the country, in this situation of surrounded by dangers, if they know nothing about the geographical situation, mountains and rivers, transportation and products, is it not different from the fact that although we have a family, we cannot know in detail how many properties there are. The great rivers and mountains will eventually be lost...".

However, we would like to raise a memorandum here, that is, competitions like map drawing must be made to achieve both universality and depth, especially the universality aspect, which should be started immediately, even if it is not possible to immediately make the national public aware of the general situation of the country, but the transportation, production, and relationship with the country of the "first line of national defense" provinces should be made clear to them in a general sense. Of course, the method does not have to be drawing maps, it can be conveyed in words or in writing.

A Visit to a Glass Factory

— Xishan

(Special Feature of This Newspaper) Glass has many uses, whether in daily utensils or in medical and chemical products, it cannot be lacking, so this is a very important industry. In recent years, although the manufacture of glass in our country has been very developed, the products are still not perfect, and the production of fine and expensive products is still sluggish, so the import of foreign glass products still reaches about 6.7 million yuan every year.

There are more than 120 factories in the country that manufacture glass, distributed in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Hubei, Henan, Shandong and other provinces, among which Shanghai is the most numerous. According to recent statistics, there are a total of 36 large and small glass manufacturing factories in the city, with a total capital of more than one million yuan, and the annual output is about four million yuan, ranking first in various places. In order to understand some of the glass manufacturing situation, I recently went to the Jinghua Glass Factory on Bailinan Road to visit.

Jinghua Factory is one of the larger glass manufacturing factories in the city, so the equipment is also very complete, and the main products are bottle shells, water cups, basins, lampshades, etc. The main raw materials are sea sand and alkali powder, etc. Most of these raw materials are domestic products. Sea sand is transported from Putuo and Zhenhai in Zhejiang; alkali powder is supplied by China Yongli Alkali Factory. Because of the good raw materials, the products are still excellent, and the average monthly output is about 120,000 yuan, ranking first among the same industry in the city.

The manufacturing process of glass, from raw materials to finished products, is divided into five steps:

(1) Raw Material Preparation: The first step in glass manufacturing is the preparation of raw materials. Because the sea sand contains a lot of moisture when it is transported, it must first be placed in a baking oven to dry it. After all the moisture is extracted, it is put into a grinding disc to grind it into extremely fine powder, and then it is mixed with alkali powder and other raw materials to dissolve into the same ingredient before being put into a steam furnace for smelting.

(2) Smelting: The next step after the preparation of materials is smelting. The factory has three steam furnaces, the largest of which is the bottle shell manufacturing furnace. It is made of fire bricks around the ten zhang square, and coated with cement and gelatinous sand, etc., because the temperature inside the furnace is extremely high, usually around 1800 degrees, so that it will not explode. There is a hopper at the top of the furnace, and the prepared raw material powder is poured in from the hopper. After a suitable smelting time, the powder becomes a fiery red liquid material, so it can start to be molded.

(3) Molding: The molding machine is connected to the outlet hopper of the smelting furnace. It can work fully automatically during manufacturing. The model of the object to be manufactured is first installed around the machine. When molding starts, the outlet hopper of the smelting furnace is opened, so that the molten liquid material is poured into each model separately. After the model is poured into a certain volume of raw material liquid, the mold shell automatically rotates upward and tilts, so that the liquid in the mold is evenly distributed to each other. After the model is complete, the mold shell automatically separates, and the formed utensils are rolled out of the machine in rows. It is said that molding with this machine is very fast, and 20 can be formed per minute, and 30,000 can be produced continuously every day.

(4) Finished Products: After the glass utensils are formed and taken out, their temperature is extremely high. If they are placed in air with uneven temperature, they will easily break, so after molding, they must be placed in a baking oven with gradually decreasing temperature to gradually reduce their heat. The area of this baking oven is 4 zhang long and 6 feet high. The temperature inside the oven is not equal from the entrance to the exit, and it is locally reduced. The initial shape is placed at the highest point of the cooked temperature, and is slowly moved until it reaches the exit, which is equal to the temperature outside the oven, so the shape can be finished.

(5) Finishing: After the utensils are finished, there will inevitably be some that are not neat, so they must be subjected to a finishing process, and check whether their composition is clear, whether the weight is balanced, and whether the model is correct, etc. Those that do not meet the standards are then beaten into powder and placed in the smelting furnace for re-smelting.

In terms of product sales, it is said that the summer of each year is relatively light, and then the production and sales situation are good. However, most products, such as glass plates and lampshades, cannot compete with imported products in the market because the manufacturing is not exquisite.

Bird Raising

— Xinye

I happened to see a hibiscus bird at a friend's house, which reminded me of my childhood: after returning home yesterday, I spent almost the entire night dreaming about raising birds.

Raising birds occupied a very important part of my childhood, because I loved raising birds in my hometown. Although I was often scolded by my mother for it, I was not discouraged. Every morning or evening, as long as my mother wasn't watching, my younger brother and I would secretly take a "trap cage" to the front of the Yuwang Temple, hang it on a large persimmon tree, and quietly hide in a cypress tree tomb, blowing a whistle commonly used by bird catchers, waiting for wild birds to enter the cage.

"Trap cage" is a sharp tool for catching birds, also made of bamboo strips: square in shape, with two trap doors on top and six trigger doors below. In the center of the cage is a decoy cage. When catching birds, first put a female bird in the decoy cage, and then insert a red object, like cherries or pomegranate seeds, on the trigger of each door. This allows it to be hung on trees in the countryside, letting the female bird call and jump in the cage. When wild birds fly over, they see their own kind calling and see these lovely red cherries, so they happily land on the cage. But without realizing it, the trigger flips, and they fall into the cage helplessly—in fact, they have been tricked; these red cherries are made of stone or evergreen seeds.

We hung the "trap cage" high in the tree, while we held our breath and squatted in the cypress tree tomb to watch. Strangely enough, our whistle was very effective. As long as we blew a few times, a large flock of birds would fly over every time, hopping and calling on the nearby pomegranate trees, mulberry trees, and the large persimmon tree, very lively and happy, as if looking for their friends. At that time, our hearts were tense, hoping they would quickly jump onto the "trap cage" and fall into the trap.

Newly captured birds, because they are not used to the cage, always thrash about in the cage without eating or calling, trying to break through the barriers and escape. At that time, we must wrap the cage in black cloth to prevent them from seeing the light, otherwise they will definitely jump to their deaths. However, after three or four days, once they get used to it, they will settle into this life.

New birds are not used to life in a cage, so all captured birds must first be placed in the same cage with old birds. After a certain period of time, they can be separated. However, we bird raisers are all sexist, because female birds are not good at calling. Except for being used as decoys and for teaching to eat, they are useless. Moreover, generally speaking, females of all animals are more beautiful than males, but birds are just the opposite. Males are lively and beautiful, exquisite and lovely, and they can sing, while females can only lay eggs and hatch, and they look bloated and ugly, and their calls are not very pleasant to hear. We only need to look at chickens to prove that my argument is not nonsense.

I have considerable experience in raising birds. I can distinguish the quality of bird species and know how to prevent bird diseases: perching sideways, tilting the head, jumping to the bottom of the cage, and a hoarse voice indicate inferior birds; a slender body, refined eyes, tight feathers, and a clear voice indicate superior species. But I love raising white-eyes; I don't like mynas or Chinese bulbuls, because white-eyes love cleanliness and are elegant, unlike mynas that are noisy, or Chinese bulbuls that are filthy.

Every day, besides going to school, I spend all my spare time raising birds. In the morning, I take them for walks in the wild; in the afternoon, I bathe them and change their cages, which makes me very happy. My younger brother, although he doesn't understand, likes to watch me do it. My mother and the others are not against me raising them, but are just afraid of "sin."

Every spring, I am even happier. The birds in the forest outside are calling, and the birds in our cage also happily sing mountain songs, one singing and one responding, which is really nice to hear.

But, an accident finally happened. One day, after I had gone to school, the white-eye I loved the most, which I had raised for five years, was stolen by someone. Even now, I still think about it from time to time—

Early Winter Sketches

— Lin Jia

(1) Camel Bells

In the early morning, before dawn, some yellow, massive creatures set out in the early cold with their masters. One following another, silently striding with heavy steps, carrying hundreds of pounds of burden on their backs: coal, lime, charcoal, persimmons... In addition to these, there were also dry grass in large cloth bags and steamed buns in small cloth bags, which were the food for the animals themselves and their masters. After walking a long distance, both the camels and the people were hungry. They would stop silently, their furry legs lightly shaking off the dust, their front knees slowly kneeling down, their bellies touching the ground. When the master put the fodder in front of them, their thick lips would begin to move, their mouths almost touching the edge of the basket, and their heavy eyes would turn to the sky.

The bells under their necks jingled softly. Besides the camels' chewing and the choking coughs of the camel driver swallowing food, this crisp sound was the only melody. This tone gently reverberated, spreading out like ripples on the water, entertaining the animals themselves and the weathered camel driver who was munching on steamed buns.

In that desert sea, where dust and sand flew in the air without end, when a string of camels met another team, everyone would wave their whips, and the camel drivers, as majestic as cavalry captains, would exchange a smile of mutual concern.

"You're starting early, oh—truly some good livestock."

Camel drivers always carefully observe other people's livestock, as knights admire their horses.

"Worth a hundred or so dollars each!"

Adjusting the ear flaps on their leather hats, they would stride past proudly, as if showing off their wealth.

Some camel drivers were merely employed, not owning their own livestock, but working for the owner of the camel team. In this type of camel team, not much camel bell sound could be heard. Only the first camel in the team had a bell around its neck, so the whole team of people and animals moved slowly forward, listening to this faint sound. On the rising humps, burlap bags or rope nets bounced incessantly.

"Hush..." The whip lashed through the air, and the gradually relaxed feet quickened again.

In the winter dawn, people and animals exhaled warm air into the cold, frosty air. The camel bells gradually swayed, and this sound wave suggested a determined heart trekking on a journey, unafraid of heavy snow cover, unafraid of the boundless desert sea, lightly blowing back a little echo in hardship.

Movies

Chen Boer's Trilogy in "United Hearts in Life and Death"

Losing Her Lover - Late at night, under the moonlight, a small boat is still rippling on the lake. She falls into her lover's arms, forgetting everything. The world before her belongs to the two of them. Her lover, only her lover, is the one who supports her body and mind. She is intoxicated. This dark lake, seen through her eyes, is full of joy and brightness. This is the night when her lover returned from Nanyang after being expelled for participating in the patriotic movement.

Running Through Power - The wind is howling, and the cranes are crying. "Arrest the revolutionaries!" This is the eve of the demise of the Northern Warlords. Due to an extraordinary coincidence, Boer's lover was arrested that day.

Rescue. Every method was tried, and all the money was used up. But to whom does the world belong? The powerful and wealthy. Women's connections cannot comfort or help her.

Due to the inevitable laws, her lover was sentenced to imprisonment and locked away in chains.

Participating in the Revolution - All of this has given her a new understanding, and new hopes have arisen with it. This is the inevitable result of her development, fighting and moving forward for the great liberation of mankind!

That was when the Northern rulers were ringing the final death knell!

That was when the heroic Northern Expeditionary Army was singing marching songs of triumph!

"Stubborn Stone Nodding" to Be Shown in Nanjing

Child star Freddi Bartholomew has garnered much praise since starring in "David Copperfield." The public cannot forget this clever and precocious child. Following "David Copperfield," he starred in many other blockbusters, such as "Little Lord Fauntleroy" and "Little Orphan Annie." Recently, he co-starred with Hollywood's top child stars, Jackie Cooper and Mickey Rooney, in "Stubborn Stone Nodding." The story tells of three innocent children who, under certain circumstances, become classmates in a school. This becomes the starting point for many touching and tearful events. The director is Van Dyke, the director of the famous film "San Francisco." In this film, Van Dyke uses a clever technique to lightly depict the purest and most beautiful emotions in the world, presenting them to us like a moving picture. His skill is admirable. This film is one of Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer's many blockbusters this year and is scheduled to be released at the Nanjing Grand Theater this Thursday.

Anecdotes from "Little Orphan Girl"

"Little Orphan Girl" is expected to be released in early next month. This is China's first sound blockbuster starring a child star in a leading role. Xinhua officials are proceeding with caution in the production of the film, so that Shirley Temple cannot have a monopoly.

The material for "Little Orphan Girl" depicts the plight of a child experiencing many trials and tribulations. The plot is extremely tortuous, melancholic, and full of pathos.

The lead actress, Chen Juanjuan, with her profound expressions, skilled movements, and fluent dialogue, is perfectly suited to the plot, showcasing her talent.

"Little Orphan Girl" has a scene of the police arresting thieves, filmed on location at the Municipal Public Security Bureau, capturing the majestic panoramic view of the Public Security Bureau and the heroic姿 of the police officers.

Before the premiere of "Little Orphan Girl," Xinhua officials will publish a series of comic strips of "Little Orphan Girl," written by the famous cartoonist Zhang Leping. The content includes hundreds of pictures and photos, with exquisite and lovely printing, and a novel and pleasing design.

"Little Orphan Girl" has two songs, one named "Little Orphan Girl" and the other named "Sitting in a Circle," sung by Chen Juanjuan, which are exceptionally moving.

Chen Juanjuan and Gu Er'yi in "Little Orphan Girl"

Interesting Tidbits from "Female Student"

In one scene, Tao Jin returns home from Shanghai, bringing a box of cream cake. After this scene was filmed, Ge Pangzi and Weng Shouzi were rumbling with hunger and were about to snatch the cream cake when the props manager secretly mixed pepper powder into the cake, making the two fools enjoy themselves immensely.

Chen Qixia's hairdresser styled Chen Qixia's hair in many different styles throughout the film. The production director, Shen Yaron, said to the hairdresser, "It's a pity that we didn't take a photo of each style, otherwise we could hang them in the barbershop as examples."

Leng Bo plays Tao Jin's father. Every time they rehearsed, Tao Jin would call him "Dad," and he would always answer loudly. Tao Jin thought he was deliberately trying to take advantage, so during rehearsals, he called him "Leng Bo," and only called him "Dad" during the actual filming.

Minxin News

The Minxin Actors Registration Department receives an increasing number of actor registration letters every day.

"Gate of Flesh" is expected to be fully completed by the end of this month.

Ge Zuozi was originally injured in his right foot in the play "Gate of Flesh." However, when filming a court scene a few days ago, his right foot was actually injured. He wrapped it in medicinal cloth, which was perfect for the performance and looked very realistic.

Minxin's newly purchased American recorder has arrived. It is extremely clever, and the recording and photography are absolutely synchronized. Single and double negatives, AC and DC power can be applied at will. "New Humanitarianism" will be filmed and recorded with this machine. This machine is said to be the latest model.

"Gate of Flesh" is special and is currently being prepared.

"New Humanitarianism" is currently filming a hospital scene, in which the character Liu Fuweng, Liu Xiang, on his deathbed, suddenly hears a speech about saving disaster victims, and then changes his will, diverting the property given to his daughter to disaster relief. But before he could sign it, he died. Compared to the original silent "Humanitarianism," it is truly incomparable. The main actors speaking out are Hu Rong, Li Junpan, and many temporary actors.

Jin Qingyu's "Reading Record" is a national defense film about brothers reading on the wall and defending against foreign aggression.
